Businessman, entrepreneur and political figure (born 1971)

Elon Musk

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Elon_Musk_-_54820081119_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk_-_54820081119_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_-_54820081119_\(cropped\).jpg)

Musk in 2025

Born

Elon Reeve Musk

  
(1971-06-28) June 28, 1971 (age 54)  

[Pretoria](/wiki/Pretoria "Pretoria"), South Africa

Citizenship

.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}

*   South Africa (since 1971)
*   Canada (since 1989)
*   United States (since 2002)

Education

[University of Pennsylvania](/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania "University of Pennsylvania") ([BA](/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts "Bachelor of Arts"), [BS](/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science "Bachelor of Science"))

Occupations

*   CEO and product architect of [Tesla](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc. "Tesla, Inc.")
*   Founder, CEO, and chief engineer of [SpaceX](/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX")
*   Founder and CEO of [xAI](/wiki/XAI_\(company\) "XAI (company)")
*   Founder and CTO of [X Corp.](/wiki/X_Corp. "X Corp.")
*   Co-founder of [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink"), [the Boring Company](/wiki/The_Boring_Company "The Boring Company"), [OpenAI](/wiki/OpenAI "OpenAI"), [Zip2](/wiki/Zip2 "Zip2"), and [X.com](/wiki/X.com_\(bank\) "X.com (bank)") (part of [PayPal](/wiki/PayPal "PayPal"))
*   President of the [Musk Foundation](/wiki/Musk_Foundation "Musk Foundation")

[Independent](/wiki/Independent_Republican_\(United_States\) "Independent Republican (United States)")[\[a\]](#cite_note-1)

.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"\[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" \]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a&gt;span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a&gt;abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}}@media print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}

*   [v](/wiki/Template:Elon_Musk_series "Template:Elon Musk series")
*   [t](/wiki/Template_talk:Elon_Musk_series "Template talk:Elon Musk series")
*   [e](/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Elon_Musk_series "Special:EditPage/Template:Elon Musk series")

**Elon Reeve Musk** ([/ˈiːlɒn/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [_EE\-lon_](/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key"); born June 28, 1971) is a businessman and entrepreneur known for [his leadership](/wiki/Business_career_of_Elon_Musk "Business career of Elon Musk") of [Tesla](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc. "Tesla, Inc."), [SpaceX](/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX"), [X](/wiki/X_\(social_network\) "X (social network)"), and [xAI](/wiki/XAI_\(company\) "XAI (company)"). Musk has been the [wealthiest person in the world](/wiki/The_World%27s_Billionaires "The World's Billionaires") since 2025; as of April 2026,[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Elon_Musk&action=edit) _[Forbes](/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ estimates [his net worth](/wiki/Wealth_of_Elon_Musk "Wealth of Elon Musk") to be US$809 billion.

Born into the wealthy [Musk family](/wiki/Musk_family "Musk family") in [Pretoria](/wiki/Pretoria "Pretoria"), South Africa, Musk emigrated in 1989 to Canada; he has Canadian citizenship since his mother was born there. He received bachelor's degrees in 1997 from the [University of Pennsylvania](/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania "University of Pennsylvania") before moving to [California](/wiki/California "California") to pursue business ventures. In 1995, Musk co-founded the software company [Zip2](/wiki/Zip2 "Zip2"). Following its sale in 1999, he co-founded [X.com](/wiki/X.com_\(bank\) "X.com (bank)"), an online payment company that later merged to form [PayPal](/wiki/PayPal "PayPal"), which was acquired by [eBay](/wiki/EBay "EBay") in 2002. Musk also became an American citizen in 2002.

In 2002, Musk founded the [space technology](/wiki/Space_technology "Space technology") company SpaceX, becoming its CEO and [chief engineer](/wiki/Chief_technology_officer "Chief technology officer"); the company has since led innovations in [reusable rockets](/wiki/Reusable_rocket "Reusable rocket") and [commercial spaceflight](/wiki/Commercial_spaceflight "Commercial spaceflight"). Musk joined the automaker Tesla as an early investor in 2004 and became its CEO and product architect in 2008; it has since become a leader in [electric vehicles](/wiki/Electric_vehicle "Electric vehicle"). In 2015, he co-founded [OpenAI](/wiki/OpenAI "OpenAI") to advance [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") (AI) research, but later left; growing discontent with the organization's direction and leadership in the [AI boom](/wiki/AI_boom "AI boom") in the 2020s led him to establish xAI, which became a subsidiary of SpaceX in 2026. In 2022, [he acquired](/wiki/Acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk") the social network Twitter, [implementing significant changes](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk "Twitter under Elon Musk"), and rebranding it as X in 2023. His other businesses include the [neurotechnology](/wiki/Neurotechnology "Neurotechnology") company [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink"), which he co-founded in 2016, and the tunneling company [the Boring Company](/wiki/The_Boring_Company "The Boring Company"), which he founded in 2017. In November 2025, a Tesla pay package worth $1 trillion for Musk was approved, which he is to receive over 10 years if he meets specific goals.

Musk is a supporter of global [far-right](/wiki/Far-right "Far-right") politics, figures, and political parties. He was the largest donor in the [2024 U.S. presidential election](/wiki/2024_U.S._presidential_election "2024 U.S. presidential election"), where he supported [Donald Trump](/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"). After Trump was inaugurated as president in January 2025, Musk served as [Senior Advisor to the President](/wiki/Senior_Advisor_to_the_President "Senior Advisor to the President") and as the _[de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto")_ head of the [Department of Government Efficiency](/wiki/Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Department of Government Efficiency") (DOGE). Shortly before [a public feud with Trump](/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Musk_feud "Trump–Musk feud"), Musk left the Trump administration in May 2025 and returned to managing his companies.

[Musk's political activities](/wiki/Political_activities_of_Elon_Musk "Political activities of Elon Musk"), statements and [views](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk "Views of Elon Musk") have made him [a polarizing figure](/wiki/Public_image_of_Elon_Musk "Public image of Elon Musk"). He has been criticized for making unscientific and misleading statements, including spreading [COVID-19 misinformation](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#COVID-19_pandemic "Views of Elon Musk"), [promoting conspiracy theories](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#Conspiracy_theories "Views of Elon Musk"), and [affirming antisemitic](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#Race_and_white_nationalism "Views of Elon Musk"), racist, and [transphobic comments](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#Transgender_issues "Views of Elon Musk"). His acquisition of Twitter was controversial due to [a subsequent increase in hate speech](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk#Increase_in_hate_speech "Twitter under Elon Musk") and the [spread of misinformation on the service](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk#Handling_of_misinformation_and_disinformation "Twitter under Elon Musk"), following his pledge to decrease [censorship](/wiki/Censorship "Censorship"). His role in the [second Trump administration](/wiki/Second_Trump_administration "Second Trump administration") attracted [public backlash](/wiki/Protests_against_Elon_Musk "Protests against Elon Musk"), particularly in [response to DOGE](/wiki/Response_to_the_Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Response to the Department of Government Efficiency"). The emails Musk sent to [Jeffrey Epstein](/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein "Jeffrey Epstein") are included in the [Epstein files](/wiki/Epstein_files "Epstein files"), which were published in 2025 and 2026 and became a topic of worldwide debate.

Early life
-

See also: [Musk family](/wiki/Musk_family "Musk family")

Elon Reeve Musk was born on June 28, 1971, in [Pretoria](/wiki/Pretoria "Pretoria"), South Africa's administrative capital.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Eligon-2022-4)[\[3\]](#cite_note-5) He is of British and [Pennsylvania Dutch](/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch "Pennsylvania Dutch") ancestry.[\[4\]](#cite_note-sjmn20140411-6)[\[5\]](#cite_note-7) His mother, [Maye](/wiki/Maye_Musk "Maye Musk") ([née](/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names "Birth name") Haldeman), is a model and dietitian born in [Saskatchewan](/wiki/Saskatchewan "Saskatchewan"), Canada, and raised in South Africa.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Biog-8)[\[7\]](#cite_note-9)[\[8\]](#cite_note-Usborne-2018-10) Musk therefore holds both South African and Canadian citizenship from birth.[\[9\]](#cite_note-11) His father, [Errol Musk](/wiki/Errol_Musk "Errol Musk"), is a South African [electromechanical engineer](/wiki/Electromechanics "Electromechanics"), pilot, sailor, consultant, [emerald](/wiki/Emerald "Emerald") dealer, and property developer, who partly owned a rental lodge at [Timbavati Private Nature Reserve](/wiki/Timbavati_Private_Nature_Reserve "Timbavati Private Nature Reserve").[\[10\]](#cite_note-Isaacson-12)[\[11\]](#cite_note-13)[\[12\]](#cite_note-NewYorker2009-14)[\[13\]](#cite_note-Smith-15)

His maternal grandfather, [Joshua N. Haldeman](/wiki/Joshua_N._Haldeman "Joshua N. Haldeman"), who died in a plane crash when Elon was a toddler, was an American-born Canadian chiropractor, aviator and political activist in the [Technocracy movement](/wiki/Technocracy_movement "Technocracy movement")[\[14\]](#cite_note-16)[\[15\]](#cite_note-:8-17) who moved to South Africa in 1950.[\[16\]](#cite_note-McGreal-18) Haldeman's anti-government, anti-democratic and conspiracist views, which included the promotion of far-right antisemitic conspiracy theories,[\[17\]](#cite_note-19)[\[18\]](#cite_note-Benton2-20) "fanatical" support of [apartheid](/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid"),[\[18\]](#cite_note-Benton2-20) and according to Errol Musk, support of [Nazism](/wiki/Nazism "Nazism"),[\[16\]](#cite_note-McGreal-18) have been suggested as an [influence on Elon](/wiki/Joshua_N._Haldeman#Influence_on_Elon_Musk "Joshua N. Haldeman").[\[19\]](#cite_note-:03-21)[\[20\]](#cite_note-22)[\[21\]](#cite_note-:13-23)[\[22\]](#cite_note-24) During his childhood, Elon was told stories by his grandmother of Haldeman's travels and exploits, and Elon has suggested that all of Haldeman's descendants have his "desire for adventure, exploration – doing crazy things".[\[23\]](#cite_note-25)

Elon has a younger brother, [Kimbal](/wiki/Kimbal_Musk "Kimbal Musk"), a younger sister, [Tosca](/wiki/Tosca_Musk "Tosca Musk"), and four paternal half-siblings.[\[24\]](#cite_note-26)[\[25\]](#cite_note-27)[\[8\]](#cite_note-Usborne-2018-10)[\[26\]](#cite_note-28) Musk was [baptized](/wiki/Baptism "Baptism") as a child in the [Anglican Church of Southern Africa](/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Southern_Africa "Anglican Church of Southern Africa").[\[27\]](#cite_note-Higgins2024-29)[\[28\]](#cite_note-Rees2024-30) The Musk family was wealthy during Elon's youth.[\[13\]](#cite_note-Smith-15) Despite both Elon and Errol previously stating that Errol was a part owner of a Zambian emerald mine,[\[13\]](#cite_note-Smith-15) in 2023, Errol recounted that the deal he made was to receive "a portion of the emeralds produced at three small mines".[\[29\]](#cite_note-31)[\[30\]](#cite_note-32) Errol was elected to the Pretoria City Council as a representative of the anti-apartheid [Progressive Party](/wiki/Progressive_Party_\(South_Africa\) "Progressive Party (South Africa)") and has said that his children shared their father's dislike of [apartheid](/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid").[\[2\]](#cite_note-Eligon-2022-4)

After his parents divorced in 1979, Elon, aged around 9, chose to live with his father because he had an _[Encyclopædia Britannica](/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica "Encyclopædia Britannica")_ set and a computer.[\[31\]](#cite_note-33)[\[4\]](#cite_note-sjmn20140411-6)[\[10\]](#cite_note-Isaacson-12) Elon later regretted his decision and became estranged from his father.[\[32\]](#cite_note-rollingstone20171115-34) Elon has recounted trips to a wilderness school that he described as a "paramilitary _[Lord of the Flies](/wiki/Lord_of_the_Flies "Lord of the Flies")_" where "bullying was a virtue" and children were encouraged to fight over rations.[\[33\]](#cite_note-35) In one incident, after an altercation with a fellow pupil, Elon was thrown down concrete steps and beaten severely, leading to him being hospitalized for his injuries.[\[34\]](#cite_note-Isaacson23-36) Elon described his father berating him after he was discharged from the hospital.[\[34\]](#cite_note-Isaacson23-36) Errol denied berating Elon and claimed, "The \[other\] boy had just lost his father to suicide, and Elon had called him stupid. Elon had a tendency to call people stupid. How could I possibly blame that child?"[\[35\]](#cite_note-Bhaimiya-37)

Elon was an enthusiastic reader of books, and had attributed his success in part to having read _[The Lord of the Rings](/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings "The Lord of the Rings")_, the [_Foundation_ series](/wiki/Foundation_\(book_series\) "Foundation (book series)"), and [_The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy_](/wiki/The_Hitchhiker%27s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_\(novel\) "The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (novel)").[\[12\]](#cite_note-NewYorker2009-14)[\[36\]](#cite_note-38) At age ten, he developed an interest in computing and video games, teaching himself how to program from the [VIC-20](/wiki/VIC-20 "VIC-20") user manual.[\[37\]](#cite_note-Vance-39) At age twelve, Elon sold his [BASIC](/wiki/BASIC "BASIC")\-based game _Blastar_ to _PC and Office Technology_ magazine for approximately $500 (equivalent to $1,600 in 2025).[\[38\]](#cite_note-play-40)[\[39\]](#cite_note-41)

### Education

[![An ornate school building](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/PBHS-facade.jpg/250px-PBHS-facade.jpg)](/wiki/File:PBHS-facade.jpg)

Musk graduated from [Pretoria Boys High School](/wiki/Pretoria_Boys_High_School "Pretoria Boys High School") in South Africa.

Musk attended [Waterkloof House Preparatory School](/wiki/Waterkloof_House_Preparatory_School "Waterkloof House Preparatory School"), [Bryanston High School](/wiki/Bryanston_High_School "Bryanston High School"), and then [Pretoria Boys High School](/wiki/Pretoria_Boys_High_School "Pretoria Boys High School"), where he graduated.[\[40\]](#cite_note-slate20191204-42) Musk was a decent but unexceptional student, earning a 61/100 in [Afrikaans](/wiki/Afrikaans "Afrikaans") and a B on his senior math certification.[\[41\]](#cite_note-43) Musk applied for a Canadian passport [through](/wiki/Jus_sanguinis "Jus sanguinis") his Canadian-born mother to avoid South Africa's [mandatory military service](/wiki/Conscription_in_South_Africa "Conscription in South Africa"),[\[42\]](#cite_note-arrived-44)[\[43\]](#cite_note-45) which would have forced him to participate in the apartheid regime,[\[2\]](#cite_note-Eligon-2022-4) as well as to ease his path to immigration to the United States.[\[44\]](#cite_note-Esquire-46) While waiting for his application to be processed, he attended the [University of Pretoria](/wiki/University_of_Pretoria "University of Pretoria") for five months.[\[45\]](#cite_note-47)

Musk arrived in Canada in June 1989, connected with a second cousin in [Saskatchewan](/wiki/Saskatchewan "Saskatchewan"),[\[46\]](#cite_note-48)[\[47\]](#cite_note-49) and worked odd jobs, including at a farm and a lumber mill.[\[48\]](#cite_note-50) In 1990, he entered [Queen's University](/wiki/Queen%27s_University_at_Kingston "Queen's University at Kingston") in [Kingston, Ontario](/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario "Kingston, Ontario").[\[49\]](#cite_note-51)[\[50\]](#cite_note-52) Two years later, he transferred to the [University of Pennsylvania](/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania "University of Pennsylvania"), where he studied until 1995.[\[51\]](#cite_note-:6-53) Although Musk has said that he earned his degrees in 1995, the University of Pennsylvania did not award them until 1997 – a [Bachelor of Arts](/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts "Bachelor of Arts") in physics and a [Bachelor of Science](/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science "Bachelor of Science") in economics from the university's [Wharton School](/wiki/Wharton_School "Wharton School").[\[52\]](#cite_note-Vance368-54)[\[53\]](#cite_note-55)[\[54\]](#cite_note-VanceA1-56)[\[55\]](#cite_note-57)[\[56\]](#cite_note-58) He reportedly hosted large, ticketed house parties to help pay for tuition, and wrote a business plan for an electronic book-scanning service similar to [Google Books](/wiki/Google_Books "Google Books").[\[57\]](#cite_note-ironman-59)

In 1994, Musk held two internships in [Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley"): one at energy storage startup Pinnacle Research Institute, which investigated electrolytic [supercapacitors](/wiki/Supercapacitor "Supercapacitor") for energy storage, and another at [Palo Alto](/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California "Palo Alto, California")–based startup [Rocket Science Games](/wiki/Rocket_Science_Games "Rocket Science Games").[\[58\]](#cite_note-60)[\[59\]](#cite_note-61) In 1995, he was accepted to a graduate program in [materials science](/wiki/Materials_science "Materials science") at [Stanford University](/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University"), but did not enroll.[\[54\]](#cite_note-VanceA1-56)[\[52\]](#cite_note-Vance368-54)[\[60\]](#cite_note-Sacchetti1026-62) Musk decided to join the [Internet boom](/wiki/Dot-com_bubble "Dot-com bubble") of the 1990s, applying for a job at [Netscape](/wiki/Netscape "Netscape"), to which he reportedly never received a response.[\[61\]](#cite_note-63)[\[42\]](#cite_note-arrived-44) _[The Washington Post](/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")_ reported that Musk lacked legal authorization to remain and work in the United States after failing to enroll at Stanford.[\[60\]](#cite_note-Sacchetti1026-62) In response, Musk said he was allowed to work at that time and that his student visa transitioned to an [H1-B](/wiki/H-1B_visa "H-1B visa"). According to numerous former business associates and shareholders, Musk said he was on a student visa at the time.[\[62\]](#cite_note-64)

Business career
-

Main article: [Business career of Elon Musk](/wiki/Business_career_of_Elon_Musk "Business career of Elon Musk")

### Zip2

Main article: [Zip2](/wiki/Zip2 "Zip2")

External videos

[![video icon](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/20px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg) [Musk speaks of his early business experience during a 2014 commencement speech at University of Southern California](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=e7Qh-vwpYH8) on YouTube

In 1995, Musk, his brother [Kimbal](/wiki/Kimbal "Kimbal"), and Greg Kouri founded the web software company [Zip2](/wiki/Zip2 "Zip2") with funding from a group of angel investors.[\[63\]](#cite_note-65) They housed the venture at a small rented office in Palo Alto.[\[64\]](#cite_note-shower-66) Replying to _[Rolling Stone](/wiki/Rolling_Stone "Rolling Stone")_, Musk denounced the notion that they started their company with funds borrowed from Elon's father Errol Musk,[\[32\]](#cite_note-rollingstone20171115-34) but in a tweet, he recognized that his father contributed 10% of a later funding round.[\[65\]](#cite_note-twitterzip2-67) The company developed and marketed an Internet city guide for the newspaper publishing industry, with maps, directions, and yellow pages.[\[66\]](#cite_note-68)

According to Musk, "The website was up during the day and I was coding it at night, seven days a week, all the time."[\[64\]](#cite_note-shower-66) To impress investors, Musk built a large plastic structure around a standard computer to create the impression that Zip2 was powered by a small supercomputer.[\[67\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVance201764-69) The Musk brothers obtained contracts with _[The New York Times](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")_ and the _[Chicago Tribune](/wiki/Chicago_Tribune "Chicago Tribune"),_[\[68\]](#cite_note-70) and persuaded the board of directors to abandon plans for a merger with [CitySearch](/wiki/CitySearch "CitySearch").[\[69\]](#cite_note-71) Musk's attempts to become CEO were thwarted by the board.[\[70\]](#cite_note-72) [Compaq](/wiki/Compaq "Compaq") acquired Zip2 for $307 million in cash in February 1999 (equivalent to $590,000,000 in 2025),[\[71\]](#cite_note-73)[\[72\]](#cite_note-74) and Musk received $22 million (equivalent to $43,000,000 in 2025) for his 7-percent share.[\[73\]](#cite_note-Vance109-75)

### X.com and PayPal

Main articles: [X.com (bank)](/wiki/X.com_\(bank\) "X.com (bank)"), [PayPal](/wiki/PayPal "PayPal"), and [PayPal Mafia](/wiki/PayPal_Mafia "PayPal Mafia")

In 1999, Musk co-founded [X.com](/wiki/X.com_\(bank\) "X.com (bank)"), an online financial services and e-mail payment company.[\[74\]](#cite_note-76) The startup was one of the first [federally insured](/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation "Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation") online banks, and, in its initial months of operation, over 200,000 customers joined the service.[\[75\]](#cite_note-77) The company's investors regarded Musk as inexperienced and replaced him with [Intuit](/wiki/Intuit "Intuit") CEO Bill Harris by the end of the year.[\[76\]](#cite_note-vance86-78) The following year, X.com merged with online bank [Confinity](/wiki/Confinity "Confinity") to avoid competition.[\[64\]](#cite_note-shower-66)[\[76\]](#cite_note-vance86-78)[\[77\]](#cite_note-79) Founded by [Max Levchin](/wiki/Max_Levchin "Max Levchin") and [Peter Thiel](/wiki/Peter_Thiel "Peter Thiel"),[\[78\]](#cite_note-80) Confinity had its own money-transfer service, [PayPal](/wiki/PayPal "PayPal"), which was more popular than X.com's service.[\[79\]](#cite_note-81)

Within the merged company, Musk returned as CEO. Musk's preference for [Microsoft](/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft") software over [Unix](/wiki/Unix "Unix") created a rift in the company and caused Thiel to resign.[\[80\]](#cite_note-82) Due to resulting technological issues and lack of a cohesive business model, the board ousted Musk and replaced him with Thiel in 2000.[\[81\]](#cite_note-83)[\[c\]](#cite_note-86) Under Thiel, the company focused on the PayPal service and was renamed PayPal in 2001.[\[83\]](#cite_note-vance89-85)[\[84\]](#cite_note-87) In 2002, PayPal was acquired by [eBay](/wiki/EBay "EBay") for $1.5 billion (equivalent to $2,700,000,000 in 2025) in stock, of which Musk—the largest shareholder with 11.72% of shares—received $175.8 million (equivalent to $320,000,000 in 2025).[\[85\]](#cite_note-88)[\[86\]](#cite_note-89) In 2017, Musk purchased the domain X.com from PayPal for an undisclosed amount, stating that it had sentimental value.[\[87\]](#cite_note-90)[\[88\]](#cite_note-91)

### SpaceX

Main article: [SpaceX](/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SpaceX_CEO_Elon_Musk_visits_N%26NC_and_AFSPC_%28190416-F-ZZ999-006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-SpaceX_CEO_Elon_Musk_visits_N%26NC_and_AFSPC_%28190416-F-ZZ999-006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:SpaceX_CEO_Elon_Musk_visits_N%26NC_and_AFSPC_\(190416-F-ZZ999-006\)_\(cropped\).jpg)

Musk explains [Starship](/wiki/SpaceX_Starship "SpaceX Starship") capabilities to leaders of [North American Aerospace Defense Command](/wiki/NORAD "NORAD"), U.S. Northern Command, and [Air Force Space Command](/wiki/Space_Operations_Command "Space Operations Command") in 2019.

In 2001, Musk became involved with the nonprofit [Mars Society](/wiki/Mars_Society "Mars Society") and discussed funding plans to place a [growth-chamber for plants](/wiki/Space_farming "Space farming") on [Mars](/wiki/Mars "Mars").[\[89\]](#cite_note-92) Seeking a way to launch the greenhouse payloads into space, Musk made two unsuccessful trips to Moscow to purchase [intercontinental ballistic missiles](/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missiles "Intercontinental ballistic missiles") (ICBMs) from Russian companies [NPO Lavochkin](/wiki/NPO_Lavochkin "NPO Lavochkin") and [Kosmotras](/wiki/Kosmotras "Kosmotras"). Musk instead decided to start a company to build affordable rockets.[\[90\]](#cite_note-Vance-2015-93) With $100 million of his early fortune,[\[91\]](#cite_note-94) (equivalent to $180,000,000 in 2025) Musk founded SpaceX in May 2002 and became the company's CEO and Chief Engineer.[\[92\]](#cite_note-95)[\[93\]](#cite_note-96)

SpaceX attempted its first launch of the [Falcon 1](/wiki/Falcon_1 "Falcon 1") rocket in 2006.[\[94\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerger2021178–182-97) Although the rocket failed to reach [Earth orbit](/wiki/Geocentric_orbit "Geocentric orbit"), it was awarded a [Commercial Orbital Transportation Services](/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services "Commercial Orbital Transportation Services") program contract from [NASA](/wiki/NASA "NASA"), then led by [Mike Griffin](/wiki/Michael_D._Griffin "Michael D. Griffin").[\[95\]](#cite_note-98)[\[96\]](#cite_note-99) After two more failed attempts that nearly caused Musk to go bankrupt,[\[94\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerger2021178–182-97) SpaceX succeeded in launching the Falcon 1 into orbit in 2008.[\[97\]](#cite_note-100) Later that year, SpaceX received a $1.6 billion NASA contract (equivalent to $2,400,000,000 in 2025) for [Falcon 9](/wiki/Falcon_9 "Falcon 9")\-launched [Dragon spacecraft](/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon "SpaceX Dragon") flights to the [International Space Station](/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") (ISS), replacing the [Space Shuttle](/wiki/Space_Shuttle "Space Shuttle") after its 2011 [retirement](/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement "Space Shuttle retirement").[\[98\]](#cite_note-101) In 2012, the Dragon vehicle docked [with the ISS](/wiki/SpaceX_COTS_Demo_Flight_2 "SpaceX COTS Demo Flight 2"), a first for a commercial spacecraft.[\[99\]](#cite_note-102)

Working towards its goal of [reusable rockets](/wiki/SpaceX_reusable_launch_system_development_program "SpaceX reusable launch system development program"), in 2015 SpaceX successfully landed the [first stage](/wiki/Multistage_rocket "Multistage rocket") of a Falcon 9 on a land platform.[\[100\]](#cite_note-103) Later landings were achieved on [autonomous spaceport drone ships](/wiki/Autonomous_spaceport_drone_ship "Autonomous spaceport drone ship"), an ocean-based recovery platform.[\[101\]](#cite_note-104) In 2018, SpaceX launched the [Falcon Heavy](/wiki/Falcon_Heavy "Falcon Heavy"); the [inaugural mission](/wiki/Falcon_Heavy_test_flight "Falcon Heavy test flight") carried [Musk's personal Tesla Roadster](/wiki/Elon_Musk%27s_Tesla_Roadster "Elon Musk's Tesla Roadster") as a [dummy payload](/wiki/Boilerplate_\(spaceflight\) "Boilerplate (spaceflight)").[\[102\]](#cite_note-105)[\[103\]](#cite_note-106) Since 2019,[\[104\]](#cite_note-107) SpaceX has been developing [Starship](/wiki/SpaceX_Starship "SpaceX Starship"), a reusable, [super heavy-lift launch vehicle](/wiki/Super_heavy-lift_launch_vehicle "Super heavy-lift launch vehicle") intended to replace the Falcon 9 and Falcon Heavy.[\[105\]](#cite_note-Roulette-2022-108) In 2020, SpaceX launched its first crewed flight, the [Demo-2](/wiki/Crew_Dragon_Demo-2 "Crew Dragon Demo-2"), becoming the first private company to place astronauts into orbit and dock a crewed spacecraft with the ISS.[\[106\]](#cite_note-109) In 2024, NASA awarded SpaceX an $843 million (equivalent to $865,000,000 in 2025) contract to build a spacecraft that NASA will use to [deorbit](/wiki/Atmospheric_entry "Atmospheric entry") the ISS at the end of its lifespan.[\[107\]](#cite_note-110)

#### Starlink

Main article: [Starlink](/wiki/Starlink "Starlink")

See also: [Starlink in the Russo-Ukrainian War](/wiki/Starlink_in_the_Russo-Ukrainian_War "Starlink in the Russo-Ukrainian War")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Starlink_Mission_%2847926144123%29.jpg/250px-Starlink_Mission_%2847926144123%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Starlink_Mission_\(47926144123\).jpg)

50 Starlink satellites shortly before deployment to low Earth orbit, 2019

In 2015, SpaceX began development of the [Starlink](/wiki/Starlink "Starlink") constellation of [low Earth orbit](/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit "Low Earth orbit") satellites to provide [satellite Internet access](/wiki/Satellite_Internet_access "Satellite Internet access").[\[108\]](#cite_note-111) After the launch of prototype satellites in 2018, the first large constellation was deployed in May 2019.[\[109\]](#cite_note-NYT-20190601-112) As of May 2025[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Elon_Musk&action=edit), over 7,600 Starlink satellites are operational,[\[110\]](#cite_note-sn2674441-113) comprising 65% of all operational Earth satellites.[\[111\]](#cite_note-d933-114) The total cost of the decade-long project to design, build, and deploy the constellation was estimated by SpaceX in 2020 to be $10 billion (equivalent to $12,000,000,000 in 2025).[\[112\]](#cite_note-115)[\[d\]](#cite_note-118)

During the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine"), Musk provided free [Starlink service to Ukraine](/wiki/Starlink_in_the_Russo-Ukrainian_War "Starlink in the Russo-Ukrainian War"), permitting Internet access and communication at a yearly cost to SpaceX of $400 million (equivalent to $440,000,000 in 2025).[\[115\]](#cite_note-119)[\[116\]](#cite_note-CNN_2022-10-13-120)[\[117\]](#cite_note-121)[\[118\]](#cite_note-122)[\[119\]](#cite_note-123) However, Musk refused to block [Russian state media](/wiki/Mass_media_in_Russia "Mass media in Russia") on Starlink.[\[120\]](#cite_note-124)[\[121\]](#cite_note-125) In 2023, Musk denied Ukraine's request to activate Starlink over [Crimea](/wiki/Crimea "Crimea") to aid an attack against the Russian navy, citing fears of a nuclear response.[\[122\]](#cite_note-Copp_2023_b431-126)[\[123\]](#cite_note-127)[\[124\]](#cite_note-128)

### Tesla

Main article: [Tesla, Inc.](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc. "Tesla, Inc.")

[![Musks stands, arms crossed and grinning, before a Tesla Model S](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Elon_Musk%2C_Tesla_Factory%2C_Fremont_%28CA%2C_USA%29_%288765031426%29.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk%2C_Tesla_Factory%2C_Fremont_%28CA%2C_USA%29_%288765031426%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk,_Tesla_Factory,_Fremont_\(CA,_USA\)_\(8765031426\).jpg)

Musk next to a [Tesla Model S](/wiki/Tesla_Model_S "Tesla Model S"), 2011

[Tesla, Inc.](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc. "Tesla, Inc."), originally Tesla Motors, was incorporated in July 2003 by [Martin Eberhard](/wiki/Martin_Eberhard "Martin Eberhard") and [Marc Tarpenning](/wiki/Marc_Tarpenning "Marc Tarpenning"). Both men played active roles in the company's early development prior to Musk's involvement.[\[125\]](#cite_note-timelinefacts-129) Musk led the [Series A round](/wiki/Series_A_round "Series A round") of investment in February 2004; he invested $6.35 million (equivalent to $11,000,000 in 2025), became the majority shareholder, and joined Tesla's board of directors as chairman.[\[126\]](#cite_note-130)[\[127\]](#cite_note-131) Musk took an active role within the company and oversaw [Roadster](/wiki/Tesla_Roadster_\(first_generation\) "Tesla Roadster (first generation)") product design, but was not deeply involved in day-to-day business operations.[\[128\]](#cite_note-132) Following a series of escalating conflicts in 2007 and the [2008 financial crisis](/wiki/2008_financial_crisis "2008 financial crisis"), Eberhard was ousted from the firm.[\[129\]](#cite_note-133)\[_[page needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_\][\[130\]](#cite_note-134) Musk assumed leadership of the company as CEO and product architect in 2008.[\[131\]](#cite_note-135) A 2009 lawsuit settlement with Eberhard designated Musk as a Tesla co-founder, along with Tarpenning and two others.[\[132\]](#cite_note-CNET-136)[\[133\]](#cite_note-FastCompany-137)

Tesla began delivery of the Roadster, an electric sports car, in 2008. With sales of about 2,500 vehicles, it was the first [mass production](/wiki/Mass_production "Mass production") all-electric car to use [lithium-ion battery](/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery "Lithium-ion battery") cells.[\[134\]](#cite_note-138) Under Musk, Tesla has since launched several well-selling electric vehicles, including the four-door sedan [Model S](/wiki/Tesla_Model_S "Tesla Model S") (2012), the [crossover](/wiki/Crossover_\(automobile\) "Crossover (automobile)") [Model X](/wiki/Tesla_Model_X "Tesla Model X") (2015), the mass-market sedan [Model 3](/wiki/Tesla_Model_3 "Tesla Model 3") (2017), the crossover [Model Y](/wiki/Tesla_Model_Y "Tesla Model Y") (2020), and the pickup truck [Cybertruck](/wiki/Tesla_Cybertruck "Tesla Cybertruck") (2023).[\[135\]](#cite_note-139)[\[136\]](#cite_note-140)[\[137\]](#cite_note-141)[\[138\]](#cite_note-142)[\[139\]](#cite_note-Krisher_2023-143) The company has also constructed multiple lithium-ion battery and electric vehicle factories, called [Gigafactories](/wiki/Gigafactory "Gigafactory").[\[140\]](#cite_note-144) In 2026, [Jon McNeill](/wiki/Jon_McNeill "Jon McNeill"), who served as president of Tesla from 2015 to 2018 and oversaw a period of revenue growth from $2 billion to $20 billion, published _The Algorithm_, a book detailing the five-step operational framework used at Tesla and SpaceX.[\[141\]](#cite_note-145)

In May 2020, Musk resigned as chairman of the board as part of the settlement of a [lawsuit from the SEC](#Legal_affairs) over him tweeting that funding had been "secured" for potentially taking Tesla private.[\[142\]](#cite_note-Goldstein_27-9-18-146)[\[143\]](#cite_note-:7-147)

Since its [initial public offering](/wiki/Initial_public_offering "Initial public offering") in 2010,[\[144\]](#cite_note-148) Tesla stock has risen significantly; it became the most valuable carmaker in summer 2020,[\[145\]](#cite_note-149)[\[146\]](#cite_note-150) and it entered the [S&P 500](/wiki/S%26P_500 "S&P 500") later that year.[\[147\]](#cite_note-151)[\[148\]](#cite_note-152) In October 2021, it reached a market capitalization of $1 trillion (equivalent to $1,200,000,000,000 in 2025), the sixth company in U.S. history to do so.[\[149\]](#cite_note-153)

#### SolarCity and Tesla Energy

Main articles: [SolarCity](/wiki/SolarCity "SolarCity") and [Tesla Energy](/wiki/Tesla_Energy "Tesla Energy")

Musk provided the initial concept and financial capital for [SolarCity](/wiki/SolarCity "SolarCity"), which his cousins [Lyndon](/wiki/Lyndon_Rive "Lyndon Rive") and Peter Rive founded in 2006.[\[150\]](#cite_note-154) By 2013, SolarCity was the second largest provider of solar power systems in the United States.[\[151\]](#cite_note-155) In 2014, Musk promoted the idea of SolarCity building an advanced production facility in [Buffalo](/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York "Buffalo, New York"), New York, triple the size of the largest solar plant in the United States.[\[152\]](#cite_note-156) Construction of [the factory](/wiki/Gigafactory_New_York "Gigafactory New York") started in 2014 and was completed in 2017. It operated as a joint venture with [Panasonic](/wiki/Panasonic "Panasonic") until early 2020.[\[153\]](#cite_note-157)[\[154\]](#cite_note-158)

Tesla acquired SolarCity for $2 billion in 2016 (equivalent to $2,700,000,000 in 2025) and merged it with its battery unit to create [Tesla Energy](/wiki/Tesla_Energy "Tesla Energy"). The deal's announcement resulted in a more than 10% drop in Tesla's stock price; at the time, SolarCity was facing liquidity issues.[\[155\]](#cite_note-:5-159) Multiple shareholder groups filed a lawsuit against Musk and Tesla's directors, stating that the purchase of SolarCity was done solely to benefit Musk and came at the expense of Tesla and its shareholders.[\[156\]](#cite_note-160)[\[157\]](#cite_note-161) Tesla directors settled the lawsuit in January 2020, leaving Musk the sole remaining defendant.[\[158\]](#cite_note-162)[\[159\]](#cite_note-163) Two years later, the court ruled in Musk's favor.[\[155\]](#cite_note-:5-159)

### Neuralink

Main article: [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink")

[![Musk standing next to bulky medical equipment on a stage](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Elon_Musk_and_the_Neuralink_Future.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk_and_the_Neuralink_Future.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_and_the_Neuralink_Future.jpg)

Musk discussing a [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink") device during a live demonstration in 2020

In 2016, Musk co-founded [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink"), a [neurotechnology](/wiki/Neurotechnology "Neurotechnology") startup, with an investment of $100 million.[\[160\]](#cite_note-sew-164)[\[161\]](#cite_note-neuraverge-165) Neuralink aims to integrate the human brain with [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") (AI) by creating devices that are embedded in the brain. Such technology could enhance memory or allow the devices to communicate with software.[\[161\]](#cite_note-neuraverge-165)[\[162\]](#cite_note-166) The company also hopes to develop devices to treat neurological conditions like [spinal cord injuries](/wiki/Spinal_cord_injury "Spinal cord injury").[\[163\]](#cite_note-pig-167) In 2022, Neuralink announced that clinical trials would begin by the end of the year.[\[164\]](#cite_note-168) In September 2023, the [Food and Drug Administration](/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration "Food and Drug Administration") approved Neuralink to initiate six-year human trials.[\[165\]](#cite_note-169)

Neuralink has conducted [animal testing](/wiki/Animal_testing "Animal testing") on [macaques](/wiki/Macaque "Macaque") at the [University of California, Davis](/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis "University of California, Davis"). In 2021, the company released a video in which a macaque played the video game _[Pong](/wiki/Pong "Pong")_ via a Neuralink implant. The company's animal trials—which have caused the deaths of some monkeys—have led to claims of [animal cruelty](/wiki/Cruelty_to_animals "Cruelty to animals"). The [Physicians Committee for Responsible Medicine](/wiki/Physicians_Committee_for_Responsible_Medicine "Physicians Committee for Responsible Medicine") has alleged that Neuralink violated the [Animal Welfare Act](/wiki/Animal_Welfare_Act_of_1966 "Animal Welfare Act of 1966").[\[166\]](#cite_note-170) Employees have complained that pressure from Musk to accelerate development has led to botched experiments and unnecessary animal deaths. In 2022, a federal probe was launched into possible animal welfare violations by Neuralink.[\[167\]](#cite_note-botched_monkeys-171)\[_[needs update](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")_\]

### The Boring Company

Main article: [The Boring Company](/wiki/The_Boring_Company "The Boring Company")

[![Musk speaks to a crowd of journalists. Behind him is a lighted tunnel.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Elon_Musk_Accelerates_the_Boring_%2845716125474%29.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk_Accelerates_the_Boring_%2845716125474%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Accelerates_the_Boring_\(45716125474\).jpg)

Musk during the 2018 inauguration of the [Boring test tunnel](/wiki/Boring_test_tunnel "Boring test tunnel") in [Hawthorne, California](/wiki/Hawthorne,_California "Hawthorne, California")

In 2017, Musk founded the Boring Company to construct tunnels; he also revealed plans for specialized, underground, high-occupancy vehicles that could travel up to 150 miles per hour (240 km/h) and thus circumvent above-ground traffic in major cities.[\[168\]](#cite_note-172)[\[169\]](#cite_note-cnndogecoin-173) Early in 2017, the company began discussions with regulatory bodies and initiated construction of a 30-foot (9.1 m) wide, 50-foot (15 m) long, and 15-foot (4.6 m) deep "test trench" on the premises of SpaceX's offices, as that required no permits.[\[170\]](#cite_note-boring-174)

The [Los Angeles tunnel](/wiki/Boring_test_tunnel "Boring test tunnel"), less than two miles (3.2 km) in length, debuted to journalists in 2018. It used Tesla Model Xs and was reported to be a rough ride while traveling at suboptimal speeds.[\[171\]](#cite_note-175) Two tunnel projects announced in 2018, in Chicago and West Los Angeles, have been canceled.[\[172\]](#cite_note-176)[\[173\]](#cite_note-177) A tunnel beneath the [Las Vegas Convention Center](/wiki/Las_Vegas_Convention_Center "Las Vegas Convention Center") was completed in early 2021.[\[174\]](#cite_note-178) Local officials have approved further expansions of the tunnel system.[\[175\]](#cite_note-179)

### X Corp.

Main articles: [Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk](/wiki/Acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk") and [Twitter under Elon Musk](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk "Twitter under Elon Musk")

.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox&gt;blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote&gt;:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child&gt;:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}

[![Avatar of Elon Musk](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg/40px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_\(crop2\).jpg "Avatar of Elon Musk")

Avatar of Elon Musk [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg/20px-Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg)

**Elon Musk [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg/20px-Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Twitter_Verified_Badge.svg)** 

.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px;white-space:nowrap}(@elonmusk)

 tweeted:

> I made an offer  
> [https://sec.gov/Archives/edgar...](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/0001418091/000110465922045641/tm2212748d1_sc13da.htm)

April 14, 2022[\[176\]](#cite_note-180)

In early 2017, Musk expressed interest in buying [Twitter](/wiki/Twitter,_Inc. "Twitter, Inc.") and had questioned the platform's commitment to [freedom of speech](/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech").[\[177\]](#cite_note-181)[\[178\]](#cite_note-182)[\[179\]](#cite_note-183) By 2022, Musk had reached 9.2% stake in the company,[\[180\]](#cite_note-elder-184) making him the largest shareholder.[\[181\]](#cite_note-Bloomberg4.14.22-185)[\[e\]](#cite_note-187) Musk later agreed to a deal that would appoint him to Twitter's board of directors and prohibit him from acquiring more than 14.9% of the company.[\[183\]](#cite_note-188)[\[184\]](#cite_note-189) Days later, Musk made a $43 billion offer to buy Twitter.[\[181\]](#cite_note-Bloomberg4.14.22-185)[\[185\]](#cite_note-190) By the end of April Musk had successfully concluded his bid for approximately $44 billion.[\[186\]](#cite_note-191) This included approximately $12.5 billion in loans and $21 billion in [equity financing](/wiki/Equity_\(finance\) "Equity (finance)").[\[187\]](#cite_note-192)[\[188\]](#cite_note-193) Having backtracked on his initial decision,[\[189\]](#cite_note-194) Musk bought the company on October 27, 2022.[\[190\]](#cite_note-deal_closed-195)

Immediately after [the acquisition](/wiki/Acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk"), Musk fired several top Twitter executives including CEO [Parag Agrawal](/wiki/Parag_Agrawal "Parag Agrawal");[\[190\]](#cite_note-deal_closed-195)[\[191\]](#cite_note-196) Musk became the CEO instead.[\[192\]](#cite_note-197) [Under Elon Musk](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk "Twitter under Elon Musk"), Twitter instituted monthly subscriptions for a "[blue check](/wiki/Twitter_verification "Twitter verification")",[\[193\]](#cite_note-198)[\[194\]](#cite_note-199)[\[195\]](#cite_note-Binoy-2022-200) and laid off a significant portion of the company's staff.[\[196\]](#cite_note-201)[\[197\]](#cite_note-202) Musk lessened content moderation and hate speech also increased on the platform after his takeover.[\[198\]](#cite_note-Knight-2022-203)[\[199\]](#cite_note-independent2023-204)[\[200\]](#cite_note-Wapo-205)[\[201\]](#cite_note-206) In late 2022, Musk released [internal documents](/wiki/Twitter_Files "Twitter Files") relating to Twitter's moderation of [Hunter Biden's laptop controversy](/wiki/Hunter_Biden_laptop_controversy "Hunter Biden laptop controversy") in the lead-up to the [2020 presidential election](/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election "2020 United States presidential election").[\[202\]](#cite_note-207) Musk also promised to step down as CEO after a Twitter poll,[\[203\]](#cite_note-208)[\[204\]](#cite_note-209) and five months later, Musk stepped down as CEO and transitioned his role to [executive chairman](/wiki/Chair_\(officer\) "Chair (officer)") and [chief technology officer](/wiki/Chief_technology_officer "Chief technology officer") (CTO).[\[205\]](#cite_note-210)

Despite Musk stepping down as CEO, X continues to struggle with challenges such as viral [misinformation](/wiki/Misinformation "Misinformation"),[\[206\]](#cite_note-211) [hate speech](/wiki/Hate_speech "Hate speech"), and [antisemitism](/wiki/Antisemitism "Antisemitism") controversies.[\[207\]](#cite_note-212)[\[208\]](#cite_note-213) Musk has been accused of [trying to silence some of his critics](/wiki/Twitter_under_Elon_Musk#Lawsuits "Twitter under Elon Musk") such as [Twitch](/wiki/Twitch_\(service\) "Twitch (service)") streamer [Asmongold](/wiki/Asmongold "Asmongold"), who criticized him during one of his streams.[\[209\]](#cite_note-free-speech-214) Musk has been accused of removing their accounts' [blue checkmarks](/wiki/Twitter_verification "Twitter verification"), which hinders visibility and is considered a form of [shadow banning](/wiki/Shadow_banning "Shadow banning"),[\[210\]](#cite_note-215)[\[211\]](#cite_note-216) or suspending their accounts without justification.[\[212\]](#cite_note-217)

Other activities
-

### Hyperloop

Main articles: [Hyperloop](/wiki/Hyperloop "Hyperloop") and [Hyperloop pod competition](/wiki/Hyperloop_pod_competition "Hyperloop pod competition")

[![A long white tube about 10 feet in diameter](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hyperloop_pod_competition_tube.jpg/250px-Hyperloop_pod_competition_tube.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hyperloop_pod_competition_tube.jpg)

A tube part of the 2017 Hyperloop pod competition, sponsored by SpaceX

In August 2013, Musk announced plans for a version of a [vactrain](/wiki/Vactrain "Vactrain"), and assigned engineers from SpaceX and Tesla to design a transport system between [Greater Los Angeles](/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles "Greater Los Angeles") and the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area"), at an estimated cost of $6 billion.[\[213\]](#cite_note-218)[\[214\]](#cite_note-219) Later that year, Musk unveiled the concept, dubbed the [Hyperloop](/wiki/Hyperloop "Hyperloop"),[\[215\]](#cite_note-220) intended to make travel cheaper than any other [mode of transport](/wiki/Mode_of_transport "Mode of transport") for such long distances.[\[216\]](#cite_note-221)

### OpenAI and xAI

Main articles: [OpenAI](/wiki/OpenAI "OpenAI") and [xAI (company)](/wiki/XAI_\(company\) "XAI (company)")

In December 2015, Musk co-founded [OpenAI](/wiki/OpenAI "OpenAI"), a [not-for-profit](/wiki/Nonprofit_corporation "Nonprofit corporation") [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") (AI) research company aiming to develop [artificial general intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence "Artificial general intelligence"), intended to be safe and beneficial to humanity.[\[217\]](#cite_note-NYT_AI-222) Musk pledged $1 billion of funding to the company,[\[218\]](#cite_note-223) but only donated $50 million.[\[219\]](#cite_note-224) In 2018, Musk left the OpenAI board.[\[220\]](#cite_note-225) Since 2018, OpenAI has made significant advances in machine learning.[\[221\]](#cite_note-226) In July 2023, Musk launched the artificial intelligence company [xAI](/wiki/XAI_\(company\) "XAI (company)"), which aims to develop a [generative AI](/wiki/Generative_artificial_intelligence "Generative artificial intelligence") program that competes with existing offerings like OpenAI's [ChatGPT](/wiki/ChatGPT "ChatGPT"). Musk obtained funding from investors in SpaceX and Tesla,[\[222\]](#cite_note-227) and xAI hired engineers from Google and OpenAI.[\[223\]](#cite_note-228)

### Private jet

Main articles: [ElonJet](/wiki/ElonJet "ElonJet") and [2022 Twitter suspensions](/wiki/2022_Twitter_suspensions "2022 Twitter suspensions")

[![Avatar of Elon Musk](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg/40px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_\(crop2\).jpg "Avatar of Elon Musk")

Avatar of Elon Musk

**Elon Musk**

(@elonmusk)

 tweeted:

> Same doxxing rules apply to "journalists" as to everyone else

December 16, 2022[\[224\]](#cite_note-229)

Musk uses a private jet owned by Falcon Landing LLC, a SpaceX-linked company, and acquired a second jet in August 2020.[\[225\]](#cite_note-flight-230)[\[226\]](#cite_note-231) His heavy use of the jets and the consequent [fossil fuel](/wiki/Fossil_fuel "Fossil fuel") usage have received criticism.[\[225\]](#cite_note-flight-230)[\[227\]](#cite_note-232) Musk's flight usage is tracked on social media through [ElonJet](/wiki/ElonJet "ElonJet").[\[228\]](#cite_note-233)[\[229\]](#cite_note-WP-234)[\[230\]](#cite_note-Sky-235) In December 2022, Musk banned the ElonJet account on Twitter, and made temporary bans on the accounts of journalists that posted stories regarding the incident, including [Donie O'Sullivan](/wiki/Donie_O%27Sullivan_\(journalist\) "Donie O'Sullivan (journalist)"), [Keith Olbermann](/wiki/Keith_Olbermann "Keith Olbermann"), and journalists from _[The New York Times](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")_, _[The Washington Post](/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")_, CNN, and _[The Intercept](/wiki/The_Intercept "The Intercept").[\[231\]](#cite_note-Taylor-2022-236)_

### Grokipedia

Main article: [Grokipedia](/wiki/Grokipedia "Grokipedia")

In October 2025, Musk's company xAI launched Grokipedia, an AI-generated online encyclopedia that he promoted as an alternative to Wikipedia.[\[232\]](#cite_note-:11-237)[\[233\]](#cite_note-238) Articles on Grokipedia are generated and reviewed by xAI's [Grok](/wiki/Grok_\(chatbot\) "Grok (chatbot)") chatbot.[\[234\]](#cite_note-239)

Media coverage and academic analysis described Grokipedia as frequently reusing Wikipedia content but framing contested political and social topics in line with Musk's own views and right-wing narratives. A study by Cornell University researchers and NBC News stated that Grokipedia cites sources that are blacklisted or considered "generally unreliable" on Wikipedia, for example, the conspiracy site [Infowars](/wiki/Infowars "Infowars") and the neo-Nazi forum [Stormfront](/wiki/Stormfront_\(website\) "Stormfront (website)"). _[Wired](/wiki/Wired_\(magazine\) "Wired (magazine)")_, _[The Guardian](/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")_ and _[Time](/wiki/Time_\(magazine\) "Time (magazine)")_ criticized Grokipedia for factual errors and for presenting Musk himself in unusually positive terms while downplaying controversies.[\[232\]](#cite_note-:11-237)[\[235\]](#cite_note-240)[\[236\]](#cite_note-241)[\[237\]](#cite_note-242)

Politics
-

.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}

![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/60px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png)

This section **may be [unbalanced](/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Undue_weight "Wikipedia:Neutral point of view") toward certain viewpoints**. Please help [improve it](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Elon_Musk&action=edit) by adding information on neglected viewpoints. Relevant discussion may be found on the [talk page](/wiki/Talk:Elon_Musk "Talk:Elon Musk"). _(April 2026)_

Main article: [Political activities of Elon Musk](/wiki/Political_activities_of_Elon_Musk "Political activities of Elon Musk")

See also: [Protests against Elon Musk](/wiki/Protests_against_Elon_Musk "Protests against Elon Musk")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/P20250530DT-0013_President_Donald_Trump_participates_in_a_press_conference_with_departing_DOGE_adviser_Elon_Musk_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-P20250530DT-0013_President_Donald_Trump_participates_in_a_press_conference_with_departing_DOGE_adviser_Elon_Musk_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:P20250530DT-0013_President_Donald_Trump_participates_in_a_press_conference_with_departing_DOGE_adviser_Elon_Musk_\(cropped\).jpg)

Musk with president [Donald Trump](/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") in May 2025

Musk is an outlier among business leaders who typically avoid partisan political advocacy.[\[238\]](#cite_note-243)[\[239\]](#cite_note-244)[\[240\]](#cite_note-245) Musk was a registered [independent voter](/wiki/Independent_voter "Independent voter") when he lived in California.[\[241\]](#cite_note-NBCNewsMail-246) Historically, he has donated to both [Democrats](/wiki/Democratic_Party_\(United_States\) "Democratic Party (United States)") and [Republicans](/wiki/Republican_Party_\(United_States\) "Republican Party (United States)"),[\[242\]](#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-247) many of whom serve in states in which he has a vested interest.[\[243\]](#cite_note-Peters-2022-248) Musk supported Democrat [Barack Obama](/wiki/Barack_Obama "Barack Obama") in [2008](/wiki/2008_US_presidential_election "2008 US presidential election") and [2012](/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election "2012 United States presidential election"),[\[244\]](#cite_note-:0-249) Democrat [Hillary Clinton](/wiki/Hillary_Clinton "Hillary Clinton") in [2016](/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election "2016 United States presidential election"), and Democrat [Joe Biden](/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") in [2020](/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election "2020 United States presidential election").[\[245\]](#cite_note-250) In the [2020 Democratic Party presidential primaries](/wiki/2020_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries "2020 Democratic Party presidential primaries"), Musk endorsed candidate [Andrew Yang](/wiki/Andrew_Yang "Andrew Yang") and expressed support for Yang's proposed [universal basic income](/wiki/Universal_basic_income "Universal basic income"),[\[246\]](#cite_note-bloomberg.com-251) and endorsed [Kanye West](/wiki/Kanye_West "Kanye West")'s [2020 presidential campaign](/wiki/Kanye_West_2020_presidential_campaign "Kanye West 2020 presidential campaign").[\[247\]](#cite_note-252)

On August 5, 2021, Biden signed an [Executive Order](/wiki/Executive_order "Executive order") targeting that half of cars sold in 2030 should be electric.[\[248\]](#cite_note-:2-253) [General Motors](/wiki/General_Motors "General Motors") CEO [Mary Barra](/wiki/Mary_Barra "Mary Barra") was in attendance.[\[248\]](#cite_note-:2-253) Musk commented, "seems odd that Tesla wasn't invited."[\[249\]](#cite_note-254) Barra said in 2024 Musk never forgave not being invited.[\[250\]](#cite_note-255)[\[251\]](#cite_note-256) In 2025, former vice president [Kamala Harris](/wiki/Kamala_Harris "Kamala Harris") said that she believed that not inviting Musk was a "big mistake."[\[252\]](#cite_note-257)[\[253\]](#cite_note-258) In September 2021, Musk criticized Biden as "not the friendliest administration."[\[254\]](#cite_note-259) In December 2021, Musk publicly expressed opposition to the [Build Back Better Act](/wiki/Build_Back_Better_Act "Build Back Better Act").[\[255\]](#cite_note-260)[\[256\]](#cite_note-261)

Since 2022, his political contributions have mostly supported Republicans, with his first vote for a Republican going to [Mayra Flores](/wiki/Mayra_Flores "Mayra Flores") in the [2022 Texas's 34th congressional district special election](/wiki/2022_Texas%27s_34th_congressional_district_special_election "2022 Texas's 34th congressional district special election").[\[257\]](#cite_note-262)[\[258\]](#cite_note-263) In 2022, Musk gave over $50 million to [Citizens for Sanity](/wiki/Citizens_for_Sanity "Citizens for Sanity"), a conservative [political action committee](/wiki/Political_action_committee "Political action committee").[\[259\]](#cite_note-mattioli-264) In 2023, he supported Republican [Ron DeSantis](/wiki/Ron_DeSantis "Ron DeSantis") for the [2024 U.S. presidential election](/wiki/2024_US_presidential_election "2024 US presidential election"), giving $10 million to his campaign,[\[259\]](#cite_note-mattioli-264) and hosted DeSantis's campaign announcement on a [Twitter Spaces](/wiki/Twitter_Spaces "Twitter Spaces") event.[\[260\]](#cite_note-265)[\[261\]](#cite_note-WaPoDesantis-266)[\[262\]](#cite_note-267) From June 2023 to January 2024, Musk hosted a bipartisan set of X Spaces with Republican and Democratic candidates, including [Robert F. Kennedy Jr.](/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Jr. "Robert F. Kennedy Jr."),[\[263\]](#cite_note-268) [Vivek Ramaswamy](/wiki/Vivek_Ramaswamy "Vivek Ramaswamy"),[\[264\]](#cite_note-269) and [Dean Phillips](/wiki/Dean_Phillips "Dean Phillips").[\[265\]](#cite_note-270)

In 2024, he started supporting international [far-right](/wiki/Far-right "Far-right") political parties, activists, and causes,[\[266\]](#cite_note-Far-right=2025-271) and has shared far-right misinformation[\[267\]](#cite_note-272)[\[268\]](#cite_note-273)[\[269\]](#cite_note-274) and numerous [conspiracy theories](/wiki/Conspiracy_theories "Conspiracy theories").[\[270\]](#cite_note-275)[\[271\]](#cite_note-276) Since 2024, [his views](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk "Views of Elon Musk") have been generally described as right-wing.[\[272\]](#cite_note-277)

[![Avatar of Elon Musk](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg/40px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28crop2%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_\(crop2\).jpg "Avatar of Elon Musk")

Avatar of Elon Musk

**Elon Musk**

(@elonmusk)

 tweeted:

> I fully endorse President Trump and hope for his rapid recovery

July 13, 2024[\[273\]](#cite_note-278)

By early 2024, Musk had become a vocal and financial supporter of Donald Trump.[\[274\]](#cite_note-279) In July 2024, minutes after Trump [survived an assassination attempt](/wiki/Attempted_assassination_of_Donald_Trump_in_Pennsylvania "Attempted assassination of Donald Trump in Pennsylvania") while speaking in [Butler, Pennsylvania](/wiki/Butler,_Pennsylvania "Butler, Pennsylvania"), Musk [endorsed him for president](/wiki/List_of_Donald_Trump_2024_presidential_campaign_endorsements "List of Donald Trump 2024 presidential campaign endorsements") saying; "I fully endorse President Trump and hope for his rapid recovery."[\[275\]](#cite_note-280)[\[276\]](#cite_note-fucked-281) During the [presidential campaign](/wiki/Donald_Trump_2024_presidential_campaign "Donald Trump 2024 presidential campaign"), Musk joined Trump on stage at a campaign rally,[\[277\]](#cite_note-282) and during the campaign promoted conspiracy theories and falsehoods about Democrats, [election fraud](/wiki/Election_denial_movement_in_the_United_States "Election denial movement in the United States")[\[278\]](#cite_note-Meyer_11012024-283) and immigration, in support of Trump.[\[279\]](#cite_note-284)[\[280\]](#cite_note-285) Musk was the largest individual donor of the 2024 election.[\[281\]](#cite_note-Thadani_12062024-286) Jacob Silverman, author of the 2025 book _Gilded Rage: Elon Musk and the Radicalization of Silicon Valley_, said that the tech industry represented by Musk, Thiel, [Andreessen](/wiki/Marc_Andreessen "Marc Andreessen") and other capitalists, actually flourished under Biden, but the tech leaders chose Trump for their common ground on cultural issues.[\[282\]](#cite_note-287)

In 2023, Musk said he shunned the [World Economic Forum](/wiki/World_Economic_Forum "World Economic Forum") (WEF) because it was boring. The organization commented that they had not invited him since 2015.[\[283\]](#cite_note-288) Musk made a last-minute WEF debut in an interview with the organization's interim co-chair [Larry Fink](/wiki/Larry_Fink "Larry Fink") during the [2026 WEF](/wiki/56th_World_Economic_Forum "56th World Economic Forum").[\[284\]](#cite_note-289)[\[285\]](#cite_note-290) He also participated in [Dialog](/wiki/Dialog_\(organization\) "Dialog (organization)"), dubbed "Tech [Bilderberg](/wiki/Bilderberg_Meeting "Bilderberg Meeting")" and organized by [Peter Thiel](/wiki/Peter_Thiel "Peter Thiel") and [Auren Hoffman](/wiki/Auren_Hoffman "Auren Hoffman").[\[286\]](#cite_note-291)[\[287\]](#cite_note-292)

Starting in January 2025, Musk's international political actions and comments came under increasing scrutiny and criticism, especially from the governments and leaders of France, Germany, Norway, Spain and the United Kingdom, particularly due to his position in the [U.S. government](/wiki/Second_Trump_administration "Second Trump administration") from January to May 2025,[\[288\]](#cite_note-Musk-bids-farewell-293) as well as ownership of X.[\[289\]](#cite_note-Times-294)[\[290\]](#cite_note-European-295)[\[291\]](#cite_note-AfD-296) A February 2025 NBC News analysis found he had boosted far-right political movements to cut immigration and curtail regulation of business in at least 18 countries on six continents since 2023.[\[292\]](#cite_note-297)

In 2025, Musk contributed $19 million to the [Wisconsin Supreme Court race](/wiki/2025_Wisconsin_Supreme_Court_election "2025 Wisconsin Supreme Court election"), hoping to influence the state's future [redistricting](/wiki/Redistricting "Redistricting") efforts and its regulations governing car manufacturers and dealers.[\[293\]](#cite_note-298)[\[294\]](#cite_note-299)

### Salute at Trump's second inauguration

Main article: [Elon Musk salute controversy](/wiki/Elon_Musk_salute_controversy "Elon Musk salute controversy")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Elon_Musk%27s_Salute_at_Donald_Trump%27s_Second_Inauguration.gif/250px-Elon_Musk%27s_Salute_at_Donald_Trump%27s_Second_Inauguration.gif)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk%27s_Salute_at_Donald_Trump%27s_Second_Inauguration.gif)

Musk giving a gesture at the [second inauguration of Donald Trump](/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Donald_Trump "Second inauguration of Donald Trump") before saying "My heart goes out to you. It is thanks to you that the future of civilization is assured."[\[295\]](#cite_note-cpdxzjw9p47o-300)[\[296\]](#cite_note-nx-s1-5269719-301)

During his speech after the [second inauguration of Donald Trump](/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Donald_Trump "Second inauguration of Donald Trump"), Musk twice made a gesture interpreted by many as a [Nazi](/wiki/Nazi_salute "Nazi salute") or a fascist [Roman salute](/wiki/Roman_salute "Roman salute").[\[f\]](#cite_note-303) He thumped his right hand over his heart, fingers spread wide, and then extended his right arm out, emphatically, at an upward angle, palm down and fingers together. He then repeated the gesture to the crowd behind him. As he finished the gestures, he said to the crowd, "My heart goes out to you. It is thanks to you that the future of civilization is assured."[\[295\]](#cite_note-cpdxzjw9p47o-300)[\[296\]](#cite_note-nx-s1-5269719-301)[\[298\]](#cite_note-304)

It was widely condemned as an intentional Nazi salute in Germany,[\[299\]](#cite_note-:62-305)[\[300\]](#cite_note-Bennhold-2025-306)[\[301\]](#cite_note-307) where [making such gestures is illegal](/wiki/Strafgesetzbuch_section_86a "Strafgesetzbuch section 86a").[\[302\]](#cite_note-rbb24.de-308) The [Anti-Defamation League](/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League "Anti-Defamation League") said it was not a Nazi salute,[\[303\]](#cite_note-:12-309) but other Jewish organizations disagreed and condemned the salute.[\[304\]](#cite_note-:72-310)[\[305\]](#cite_note-:82-311)[\[306\]](#cite_note-:9-312)[\[307\]](#cite_note-:02-313) American public opinion was divided on partisan lines as to whether it was a fascist salute.[\[308\]](#cite_note-:10-314) Musk dismissed the accusations of [Nazi](/wiki/Nazi "Nazi") sympathies, deriding them as "dirty tricks" and a "tired" attack.[\[309\]](#cite_note-315)[\[310\]](#cite_note-Fortinsky-2025a-316) [Neo-Nazi](/wiki/Neo-Nazi "Neo-Nazi") and [white supremacist](/wiki/White_supremacist "White supremacist") groups celebrated it as a Nazi salute.[\[303\]](#cite_note-:12-309)[\[311\]](#cite_note-Condon-2025-317) Multiple European political parties demanded that Musk be banned from entering their countries.[\[312\]](#cite_note-318)[\[313\]](#cite_note-319)

### Department of Government Efficiency

Main article: [Department of Government Efficiency](/wiki/Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Department of Government Efficiency")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Elon_Musk_%2854350004520%29.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk_%2854350004520%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_\(54350004520\).jpg)

Elon Musk wielding a chainsaw at the [Conservative Political Action Conference](/wiki/Conservative_Political_Action_Conference "Conservative Political Action Conference") (CPAC) in 2025, imitating a publicity stunt used by [Javier Milei](/wiki/Javier_Milei "Javier Milei") symbolic of efficiency, [federal mass layoffs](/wiki/2025_United_States_federal_mass_layoffs "2025 United States federal mass layoffs") and [tax cutting](/wiki/Tax_cut "Tax cut")

The concept of DOGE emerged in a discussion between Musk and [Donald Trump](/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"), and in August 2024, Trump committed to giving Musk an advisory role, with Musk accepting the offer.[\[314\]](#cite_note-Shepardson-320) In November and December 2024, Musk suggested that the organization could help to cut the [U.S. federal budget](/wiki/United_States_federal_budget "United States federal budget"), consolidate the number of federal agencies,[\[315\]](#cite_note-321)[\[316\]](#cite_note-322) and eliminate the [Consumer Financial Protection Bureau](/wiki/Consumer_Financial_Protection_Bureau "Consumer Financial Protection Bureau"),[\[317\]](#cite_note-323)[\[318\]](#cite_note-324) and that its final stage would be "deleting itself".[\[319\]](#cite_note-325)

In January 2025, the organization was created by [executive order](/wiki/Executive_order "Executive order"), and Musk was designated a "[special government employee](/wiki/Special_government_employee "Special government employee")".[\[320\]](#cite_note-MD2-326)[\[321\]](#cite_note-Ngo_1212025-327) Musk led the organization and was a [senior advisor to the president](/wiki/Senior_Advisor_to_the_President_of_the_United_States "Senior Advisor to the President of the United States"),[\[322\]](#cite_note-328) although his [official role](/wiki/Political_activities_of_Elon_Musk "Political activities of Elon Musk") is not clear.[\[323\]](#cite_note-Wolf2-329) In sworn statement during a lawsuit, the director of the White House [Office of Administration](/wiki/Office_of_Administration "Office of Administration") stated that Musk "is not an employee of the U.S. DOGE Service or U.S. DOGE Service Temporary Organization", "is not the U.S. DOGE Service administrator", and has "no actual or formal authority to make government decisions himself".[\[324\]](#cite_note-330)[\[325\]](#cite_note-331) Trump said two days later that he had put Musk in charge of DOGE.[\[326\]](#cite_note-332) A federal judge has ruled that Musk acted as the _de facto_ leader of DOGE.[\[327\]](#cite_note-333)

Musk's role in the [second Trump administration](/wiki/Second_Trump_administration "Second Trump administration"), particularly in [response to DOGE](/wiki/Response_to_the_Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Response to the Department of Government Efficiency"), has [attracted public backlash](/wiki/Protests_against_Elon_Musk "Protests against Elon Musk"). He was criticized for his treatment of federal government employees,[\[328\]](#cite_note-nyt-young-aides-25-334)[\[329\]](#cite_note-nyt-swan-musk-feb-25-335)[\[330\]](#cite_note-wp-zs-25-336) including his influence over the [mass layoffs of the federal workforce](/wiki/2025_United_States_federal_mass_layoffs "2025 United States federal mass layoffs").[\[331\]](#cite_note-337)[\[332\]](#cite_note-338)[\[333\]](#cite_note-339) He has prioritized secrecy within the organization[\[334\]](#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-340) and has accused others of violating privacy laws.[\[320\]](#cite_note-MD2-326) A Senate report alleged that Musk could avoid up to $2 billion in legal liability as a result of DOGE's actions.[\[335\]](#cite_note-341) In May 2025, [Bill Gates](/wiki/Bill_Gates "Bill Gates") accused Musk of "killing the world's poorest children" through his cuts to [USAID](/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development "United States Agency for International Development").[\[336\]](#cite_note-342) Modeling by [Boston University](/wiki/Boston_University "Boston University") estimated the cuts resulted in 400,000 children and 200,000 adults deaths by November.[\[337\]](#cite_note-343)[\[338\]](#cite_note-344)[\[339\]](#cite_note-usaid-shutdown-345) Musk departed on May 28, 2025, when the special government employee's 130 day deadline expired.[\[340\]](#cite_note-346)[\[341\]](#cite_note-347)[\[342\]](#cite_note-348)

### Feud with Donald Trump

Main article: [Trump–Musk feud](/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Musk_feud "Trump–Musk feud")

[![Avatar of Elon Musk](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28cropped%29.jpg/40px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_\(cropped\).jpg "Avatar of Elon Musk")

Avatar of Elon Musk

**Elon Musk**

(@elonmusk)

 tweeted:

> Time to drop the really big bomb:
> 
> @realDonaldTrump is in the Epstein files. That is the real reason they have not been made public.
> 
> Have a nice day, [DJT](/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump")!

June 5, 2025[\[343\]](#cite_note-349)

After leaving office, Musk criticized the Trump administration's [Big Beautiful Bill](/wiki/One_Big_Beautiful_Bill_Act "One Big Beautiful Bill Act"), calling it a "disgusting abomination" due to its provisions increasing the deficit.[\[344\]](#cite_note-350) A feud began between Musk and Trump, with its most notable event being Musk alleging Trump had ties to sex offender [Jeffrey Epstein](/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein "Jeffrey Epstein") on X (formerly Twitter) on June 5, 2025.[\[345\]](#cite_note-Epstein1-351)[\[346\]](#cite_note-Epstein2-352) Trump responded on [Truth Social](/wiki/Truth_Social "Truth Social") stating that Musk went "CRAZY" after the "EV Mandate" was purportedly taken away and threatened to cut Musk's government contracts.[\[347\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPager2025d-353)[\[348\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPager2025e-354) Musk then called for a third Trump impeachment.[\[349\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBasu2025-355) The next day, Trump stated that he did not wish to reconcile with Musk, and added that Musk would face "very serious consequences" if he funds Democratic candidates.[\[350\]](#cite_note-356) On June 11, Musk publicly apologized for the tweets against Trump before deleting them, saying they "went too far".[\[351\]](#cite_note-357)

Views
-----

Main article: [Views of Elon Musk](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk "Views of Elon Musk")

[![Avatar of Elon Musk](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28cropped%29.jpg/40px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society_\(cropped\).jpg "Avatar of Elon Musk")

Avatar of Elon Musk

**Elon Musk**

(@elonmusk)

 tweeted:

> My commitment to free speech extends even to not banning the account following my plane, even though that is a direct personal safety risk

November 6, 2022[\[352\]](#cite_note-plane-358)

Rejecting the [conservative](/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States "Conservatism in the United States") label,[\[353\]](#cite_note-359) Musk has described himself as a [political moderate](/wiki/Political_moderate "Political moderate"), even as his views have become more [right-wing](/wiki/Right-wing "Right-wing") over time.[\[354\]](#cite_note-Right-wing-360) His views have been characterized as [libertarian](/wiki/Libertarianism_in_the_United_States "Libertarianism in the United States") and [far-right](/wiki/Far-right "Far-right"),[\[355\]](#cite_note-Libertarian-361)[\[356\]](#cite_note-Far-right-362) and after [his involvement in European politics](/wiki/Political_activities_of_Elon_Musk "Political activities of Elon Musk"), they have received criticism from world leaders such as [Emmanuel Macron](/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron "Emmanuel Macron") and [Olaf Scholz](/wiki/Olaf_Scholz "Olaf Scholz").[\[357\]](#cite_note-olaf-363)[\[358\]](#cite_note-Henley-2025-364)[\[359\]](#cite_note-365)[\[360\]](#cite_note-366)

Within the context of [American politics](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#U.S._politics "Views of Elon Musk"), Musk supported Democratic candidates up until 2022, at which point he voted for a Republican for the first time.[\[244\]](#cite_note-:0-249)[\[361\]](#cite_note-:1-367) He has stated support for [universal basic income](/wiki/Universal_basic_income "Universal basic income"),[\[362\]](#cite_note-uni2-368) [gun rights](/wiki/Gun_rights "Gun rights"),[\[363\]](#cite_note-369) [freedom of speech](/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech"),[\[364\]](#cite_note-370) a [tax on carbon emissions](/wiki/Tax_on_carbon_emissions "Tax on carbon emissions"),[\[365\]](#cite_note-371) and [H-1B visas](/wiki/H-1B_visa "H-1B visa").[\[366\]](#cite_note-CBS_News-2024-372) Musk has expressed concern about issues such as [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") (AI)[\[367\]](#cite_note-wp2015-373) and [climate change](/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change"),[\[368\]](#cite_note-374) and has been a critic of [wealth tax](/wiki/Wealth_tax "Wealth tax"),[\[369\]](#cite_note-375) [short-selling](/wiki/Short-selling "Short-selling"),[\[370\]](#cite_note-376) and [government subsidies](/wiki/Government_subsidies "Government subsidies").[\[371\]](#cite_note-377) An immigrant himself, Musk has been accused of being [anti-immigration](/wiki/Anti-immigration "Anti-immigration"), and regularly blames [immigration policies](/wiki/Immigration_policy_of_the_United_States "Immigration policy of the United States") for [illegal immigration](/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States "Illegal immigration to the United States").[\[372\]](#cite_note-Fearmongering-378) He is also a [pronatalist](/wiki/Pronatalist "Pronatalist") who believes [population decline](/wiki/Population_decline "Population decline") is the biggest threat to civilization,[\[373\]](#cite_note-Pronatlist-379) and identifies as a [cultural Christian](/wiki/Cultural_Christian "Cultural Christian").[\[374\]](#cite_note-O'Mahony2024-380)[\[375\]](#cite_note-381) Musk has long been an advocate for [space colonization](/wiki/Space_colonization "Space colonization"), especially the [colonization of Mars](/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars "Colonization of Mars"). He has repeatedly pushed for humanity colonizing Mars, in order to become an interplanetary species and lower the risks of [human extinction](/wiki/Human_extinction "Human extinction").[\[376\]](#cite_note-SpaceX-382)
