Musk has [promoted conspiracy theories](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#Conspiracy_theories "Views of Elon Musk") and [made controversial statements](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk#Race_and_white_nationalism "Views of Elon Musk") that have led to accusations of [racism](/wiki/Racism "Racism"), [sexism](/wiki/Sexism "Sexism"), [antisemitism](/wiki/Antisemitism "Antisemitism"),[\[377\]](#cite_note-383)[\[378\]](#cite_note-Truth-384) [transphobia](/wiki/Transphobia "Transphobia"),[\[379\]](#cite_note-385) disseminating [disinformation](/wiki/Disinformation "Disinformation"), and support of [white pride](/wiki/White_pride "White pride").[\[380\]](#cite_note-Proud-386)[\[381\]](#cite_note-Derbyshire-2025-387) While describing himself as a "pro-Semite",[\[382\]](#cite_note-CNBC160523-388) his comments regarding [George Soros](/wiki/George_Soros "George Soros") and [Jewish communities](/wiki/Jewish_communities "Jewish communities") have been condemned by the [Anti-Defamation League](/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League "Anti-Defamation League") and the Biden [White House](/wiki/White_House "White House").[\[383\]](#cite_note-Condemned-389) Musk was criticized during the COVID-19 pandemic for making unfounded epidemiological claims,[\[384\]](#cite_note-kolodny-2020a-390) defying [COVID-19 lockdowns](/wiki/COVID-19_lockdowns "COVID-19 lockdowns") restrictions,[\[385\]](#cite_note-:3-391) and supporting the [Canada convoy protest](/wiki/Canada_convoy_protest "Canada convoy protest") against [vaccine mandates](/wiki/COVID-19_vaccine_mandates "COVID-19 vaccine mandates").[\[386\]](#cite_note-392)[\[387\]](#cite_note-393) He has amplified false claims of [white genocide](/wiki/White_genocide_conspiracy_theory#South_Africa "White genocide conspiracy theory") in South Africa.[\[388\]](#cite_note-394)

### International relations

Main article: [International relations of Elon Musk](/wiki/International_relations_of_Elon_Musk "International relations of Elon Musk")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Isaac_Herzog_in_Beit_HaNassi%2C_November_2023_%28GPOHZ02222_2%29.jpeg/250px-Isaac_Herzog_in_Beit_HaNassi%2C_November_2023_%28GPOHZ02222_2%29.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Isaac_Herzog_in_Beit_HaNassi,_November_2023_\(GPOHZ02222_2\).jpeg)

Musk with Israeli president [Isaac Herzog](/wiki/Isaac_Herzog "Isaac Herzog"), November 2023

Musk has been critical of Israel's [actions](/wiki/Israeli_invasion_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Israeli invasion of the Gaza Strip") in the [Gaza Strip](/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip") during the [Gaza war](/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war"),[\[389\]](#cite_note-Robertson-20232-395) praised China's economic and climate goals,[\[390\]](#cite_note-He-20212-396)[\[391\]](#cite_note-Choi-20192-397) suggested that [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") and China should resolve [cross-strait relations](/wiki/Cross-strait_relations "Cross-strait relations"),[\[392\]](#cite_note-Liang-20222-398)[\[393\]](#cite_note-Khalaf-20222-399) and was described as having a close relationship with the [Chinese government](/wiki/Chinese_government "Chinese government").[\[390\]](#cite_note-He-20212-396)[\[391\]](#cite_note-Choi-20192-397)

In Europe, Musk expressed support for Ukraine in 2022 during the [Russian invasion](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine"), recommended referendums and peace deals on the annexed [Russia-occupied territories](/wiki/Russian-occupied_territories_of_Ukraine "Russian-occupied territories of Ukraine"),[\[394\]](#cite_note-Oshin-20222-400)[\[395\]](#cite_note-Wilson-20222-401) and supported the far-right [Alternative for Germany](/wiki/Alternative_for_Germany "Alternative for Germany") political party in 2024.[\[396\]](#cite_note-Gold-20242-402)

Regarding [British politics](/wiki/British_politics "British politics"), Musk blamed the [2024 UK riots](/wiki/2024_United_Kingdom_riots "2024 United Kingdom riots") on [mass migration](/wiki/Modern_immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom "Modern immigration to the United Kingdom") and [open borders](/wiki/Open_border "Open border"),[\[397\]](#cite_note-Gregory-20242-403)[\[398\]](#cite_note-BBC_News-2024a2-404) criticized Prime Minister [Keir Starmer](/wiki/Keir_Starmer "Keir Starmer") for what he described as a "two-tier" policing system,[\[399\]](#cite_note-The_Independent-20242-405)[\[400\]](#cite_note-The_Daily_Telegraph-20242-406)[\[398\]](#cite_note-BBC_News-2024a2-404) and was subsequently attacked as being responsible for spreading [misinformation](/wiki/Misinformation "Misinformation") and amplifying the far-right.[\[401\]](#cite_note-BBC_News2-407) He has also voiced his support for far-right UK activist [Tommy Robinson](/wiki/Tommy_Robinson "Tommy Robinson") and pledged electoral support for [Reform UK](/wiki/Reform_UK "Reform UK").[\[402\]](#cite_note-BBC_News-20252-408)[\[403\]](#cite_note-Turvill-20242-409)

In February 2026, Musk described Spanish Prime Minister [Pedro Sánchez](/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez "Pedro Sánchez") as a "tyrant" following Sánchez's proposal to [prohibit minors](/wiki/Social_media_age_verification_laws_by_country#Spain "Social media age verification laws by country") under the age of 16 from accessing social media platforms.[\[404\]](#cite_note-410)

Legal affairs
-

Main article: [Legal affairs of Elon Musk](/wiki/Legal_affairs_of_Elon_Musk "Legal affairs of Elon Musk")

Further information: [List of lawsuits involving Tesla, Inc.](/wiki/List_of_lawsuits_involving_Tesla,_Inc. "List of lawsuits involving Tesla, Inc.") and [Criticism of Tesla, Inc.](/wiki/Criticism_of_Tesla,_Inc. "Criticism of Tesla, Inc.")

In 2018, Musk was [sued](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc.#Lawsuits_and_controversies "Tesla, Inc.") by the [U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission](/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission "U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission") (SEC) for a [tweet](/wiki/Tweet_\(social_media\) "Tweet (social media)") stating that funding had been secured for potentially taking Tesla private.[\[142\]](#cite_note-Goldstein_27-9-18-146)[\[g\]](#cite_note-414) The securities fraud lawsuit characterized the tweet as false, misleading, and damaging to investors, and sought to bar Musk from serving as CEO of [publicly traded companies](/wiki/Public_company "Public company").[\[142\]](#cite_note-Goldstein_27-9-18-146)[\[408\]](#cite_note-415)[\[409\]](#cite_note-OkaneLopatto18-416) Two days later, Musk settled with the SEC, without admitting or denying the SEC's allegations. As a result, Musk and Tesla were fined $20 million each, and Musk was forced to step down for three years as Tesla chairman but was able to remain as CEO.[\[143\]](#cite_note-:7-147) Shareholders filed a lawsuit over the tweet,[\[410\]](#cite_note-417) and in February 2023, a jury found Musk and Tesla not liable.[\[411\]](#cite_note-418) Musk has stated in interviews that he does not regret posting the tweet that triggered the SEC investigation.[\[412\]](#cite_note-419)[\[413\]](#cite_note-420)

In 2019, Musk stated in a tweet that Tesla would build half a million cars that year.[\[414\]](#cite_note-421) The SEC reacted by asking a court to hold him [in contempt](/wiki/Contempt_of_court "Contempt of court") for violating the terms of the 2018 settlement agreement. A joint agreement between Musk and the SEC eventually clarified the previous agreement details,[\[415\]](#cite_note-422) including a list of topics about which Musk needed preclearance.[\[416\]](#cite_note-423) In 2020, a judge blocked a lawsuit that claimed a tweet by Musk regarding Tesla stock price ("too high [imo](/wiki/List_of_acronyms:_I "List of acronyms: I")") violated the agreement.[\[417\]](#cite_note-424)[\[418\]](#cite_note-425) [Freedom of Information Act](/wiki/Freedom_of_Information_Act_\(United_States\) "Freedom of Information Act (United States)") (FOIA)-released records showed that the SEC concluded Musk had subsequently violated the agreement twice by tweeting regarding "[Tesla's solar roof](/wiki/Tesla_Energy "Tesla Energy") production volumes and its stock price".[\[419\]](#cite_note-426)

In October 2023, the SEC sued Musk over his refusal to testify a third time in an investigation into whether he violated federal law by purchasing Twitter stock in 2022.[\[420\]](#cite_note-Brodkin-2023-427)[\[421\]](#cite_note-428)[\[422\]](#cite_note-Regulator_sues_Musk_to_force_testimony_in_X_probe-2023-429) In February 2024, Judge Laurel Beeler ruled that Musk must testify again.[\[423\]](#cite_note-430) In January 2025, the SEC filed a lawsuit against Musk for securities violations related to his purchase of Twitter.[\[424\]](#cite_note-431)

In January 2024, Delaware judge [Kathaleen McCormick](/wiki/Kathaleen_McCormick "Kathaleen McCormick") ruled in a 2018 lawsuit that Musk's $55 billion pay package from Tesla be rescinded.[\[425\]](#cite_note-432) McCormick called the compensation granted by the company's board "an unfathomable sum" that was unfair to shareholders.[\[426\]](#cite_note-433) The [Delaware Supreme Court](/wiki/Delaware_Supreme_Court "Delaware Supreme Court") overturned McCormick's decision in December 2025, restoring Musk's compensation package and awarding $1 in [nominal damages](/wiki/Nominal_damages "Nominal damages").[\[427\]](#cite_note-434)

On March 20, 2026, a jury in [San Francisco, California](/wiki/San_Francisco,_California "San Francisco, California"), found Musk liable for misleading investors during his [acquisition of Twitter](/wiki/Acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk"), though they absolved him of some fraud allegations, finding he did not "scheme" to defraud investors.[\[428\]](#cite_note-misleadverdict-435)[\[429\]](#cite_note-lat-jury-finds-elon-musk-misled-investors-during-twitter-purchase-436) Specifically, Musk was found to have misled shareholders in two tweets, but not in a podcast, as the views he expressed in that were deemed by the jury to be an opinion.[\[428\]](#cite_note-misleadverdict-435)[\[429\]](#cite_note-lat-jury-finds-elon-musk-misled-investors-during-twitter-purchase-436) Damages have yet to be calculated, but plaintiffs' lawyers estimated them to be $2.5 billion.[\[430\]](#cite_note-437)

[Jury selection](/wiki/Jury_selection "Jury selection") for Musk's [lawsuit](/wiki/Musk_v._Altman "Musk v. Altman") against OpenAI and its current executives, including [Sam Altman](/wiki/Sam_Altman "Sam Altman") and [Greg Brockman](/wiki/Greg_Brockman "Greg Brockman"), began on April 27, 2026.[\[431\]](#cite_note-438)[\[432\]](#cite_note-439) On April 28, 2026, trial testimony was by now underway, with Elon Musk beginning his testimony against Altman and OpenAI.[\[433\]](#cite_note-440) On April 30, 2026 Musk would enter his third day of testimony.[\[434\]](#cite_note-441)

Personal life
-

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Elon_Musk_Royal_Society.jpg/250px-Elon_Musk_Royal_Society.jpg)](/wiki/File:Elon_Musk_Royal_Society.jpg)

Official [Royal Society](/wiki/Royal_Society "Royal Society") portrait, 2018

Musk became a U.S. citizen in 2002.[\[51\]](#cite_note-:6-53) From the early 2000s until late 2020, Musk resided in California, where both Tesla and SpaceX were founded.[\[435\]](#cite_note-bloomberg20201208-442) He then relocated to [Cameron County, Texas](/wiki/Cameron_County,_Texas "Cameron County, Texas"),[\[436\]](#cite_note-443)[\[437\]](#cite_note-444) saying that California had become "complacent" about its economic success.[\[435\]](#cite_note-bloomberg20201208-442)[\[438\]](#cite_note-445)[\[439\]](#cite_note-446)

While hosting _[Saturday Night Live](/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live "Saturday Night Live")_ in 2021, Musk stated that he has [Asperger syndrome](/wiki/Asperger_syndrome "Asperger syndrome") (an outdated term for a mild strain of [autism spectrum disorder](/wiki/Autism "Autism")), although he has never been formally diagnosed.[\[440\]](#cite_note-447)[\[441\]](#cite_note-448) When asked about his experience growing up with Asperger's syndrome in a [TED conference](/wiki/TED_\(conference\) "TED (conference)") in Vancouver in 2022, Musk stated that "the social cues were not intuitive ... I would just tend to take things very literally ... but then that turned out to be wrong — \[people were not\] simply saying exactly what they mean, there's all sorts of other things that are meant, and \[it\] took me a while to figure that out."[\[442\]](#cite_note-449) Musk suffers from back pain and has undergone several spine-related surgeries, including a [disc](/wiki/Intervertebral_disc "Intervertebral disc") replacement.[\[443\]](#cite_note-450)[\[444\]](#cite_note-451) In 2000, he contracted a severe case of [malaria](/wiki/Malaria "Malaria") while on vacation in South Africa.[\[445\]](#cite_note-452)

Musk has stated he uses doctor-prescribed [ketamine](/wiki/Ketamine "Ketamine") for occasional depression and that he doses "a small amount once every other week or something like that";[\[446\]](#cite_note-453) since January 2024, some media outlets have reported that he takes ketamine, [marijuana](/wiki/Marijuana "Marijuana"), [LSD](/wiki/LSD "LSD"), [ecstasy](/wiki/Ecstasy_\(drug\) "Ecstasy (drug)"), [mushrooms](/wiki/Hallucinogenic_mushrooms "Hallucinogenic mushrooms"), [cocaine](/wiki/Cocaine "Cocaine") and other drugs. Musk at first refused to comment on his alleged drug use, before responding that he had not [tested](/wiki/Drug_test "Drug test") positive for drugs, and that if drugs somehow improved his productivity, "I would definitely take them!".[\[447\]](#cite_note-454) _[The New York Times'](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")_ investigations revealed Musk's overuse of ketamine and numerous other drugs, as well as strained family relationships and concerns from close associates who have become troubled by his public behavior as he became more involved in political activities and government work.[\[448\]](#cite_note-455) According to _The Washington Post_, President Trump described Musk as "a big-time drug addict".[\[449\]](#cite_note-456)

Through his own label Emo G Records, Musk released a [rap](/wiki/Rap "Rap") track, "RIP [Harambe](/wiki/Harambe "Harambe")", on [SoundCloud](/wiki/SoundCloud "SoundCloud") in March 2019.[\[450\]](#cite_note-457)[\[451\]](#cite_note-458)[\[452\]](#cite_note-Fitzgerald-459) The following year, he released an [EDM](/wiki/Electronic_dance_music "Electronic dance music") track, "Don't Doubt Ur Vibe", featuring his own lyrics and vocals.[\[453\]](#cite_note-Etherington-460)

Musk plays video games, which he stated has a "'restoring effect' that helps his 'mental calibration'".[\[454\]](#cite_note-461) Some games he plays include [_Quake_](/wiki/Quake_\(series\) "Quake (series)"), _[Diablo IV](/wiki/Diablo_IV "Diablo IV")_, _[Elden Ring](/wiki/Elden_Ring "Elden Ring")_, and [_Polytopia_](/wiki/The_Battle_of_Polytopia "The Battle of Polytopia").[\[455\]](#cite_note-462)[\[456\]](#cite_note-463) Musk once claimed to be one of the world's top video game players but has since admitted to "[account boosting](/wiki/Boosting_\(video_games\) "Boosting (video games)")", or cheating by hiring outside services to achieve top player rankings.[\[457\]](#cite_note-464)[\[458\]](#cite_note-465)[\[459\]](#cite_note-Gizmodo_Paying-466) Musk has justified the boosting by claiming that all top accounts do it so he has to as well to remain competitive.[\[460\]](#cite_note-467)[\[459\]](#cite_note-Gizmodo_Paying-466)[\[461\]](#cite_note-468) In 2024 and 2025, Musk criticized the video game _[Assassin's Creed Shadows](/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_Shadows "Assassin's Creed Shadows")_ and its creator [Ubisoft](/wiki/Ubisoft "Ubisoft") for "woke" content.[\[462\]](#cite_note-PC_Gamer_Ratio-469) Musk posted to X that "DEI kills art" and specified the inclusion of the historical figure [Yasuke](/wiki/Yasuke "Yasuke") in the _Assassin's Creed_ game as offensive; he also called the game "terrible". Ubisoft responded by saying that Musk's comments were "just feeding hatred" and that they were focused on producing a game not pushing politics.[\[463\]](#cite_note-470)[\[464\]](#cite_note-471)

### Relationships and children

Further information: [Musk family](/wiki/Musk_family "Musk family")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/X_%C3%86_A-Xii%2C_Elon_Musk_and_Donald_Trump_in_the_Oval_Office_-_P20250207DT-0103_%2854320797642%29.jpg/250px-X_%C3%86_A-Xii%2C_Elon_Musk_and_Donald_Trump_in_the_Oval_Office_-_P20250207DT-0103_%2854320797642%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:X_%C3%86_A-Xii,_Elon_Musk_and_Donald_Trump_in_the_Oval_Office_-_P20250207DT-0103_\(54320797642\).jpg)

Musk with his son, X Æ A-Xii, in the [Oval Office](/wiki/Oval_Office "Oval Office") on February 11, 2025

Musk has fathered at least 14 children, one of whom died as an infant.[\[465\]](#cite_note-472) _The Wall Street Journal_ reported in 2025 that sources close to Musk suggest that the "true number of Musk's children is much higher than publicly known".[\[1\]](#cite_note-Mattioli_16APR2025-2) He had six children with his first wife, Canadian author [Justine Wilson](/wiki/Justine_Wilson "Justine Wilson"), whom he met while attending Queen's University in Ontario, Canada; they married in 2000.[\[466\]](#cite_note-Streisand-2015-473) In 2002, their first child, Nevada Alexander Musk, died of [sudden infant death syndrome](/wiki/Sudden_infant_death_syndrome "Sudden infant death syndrome") at the age of 10 days.[\[467\]](#cite_note-sids-474) After his death, the couple used [in vitro fertilization](/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation "In vitro fertilisation") (IVF) to continue their family;[\[468\]](#cite_note-holywoodlife2021-475) they had twins in 2004, followed by triplets in 2006.[\[468\]](#cite_note-holywoodlife2021-475) The couple divorced in 2008 and have [shared custody](/wiki/Joint_custody_\(United_States\) "Joint custody (United States)") of their children.[\[469\]](#cite_note-476)[\[470\]](#cite_note-477) The elder twin he had with Wilson [came out](/wiki/Gender_identity "Gender identity") as a [trans woman](/wiki/Trans_woman "Trans woman") and, in 2022, officially [changed her name](/wiki/Name_change "Name change") to [Vivian Jenna Wilson](/wiki/Vivian_Wilson "Vivian Wilson"),[\[471\]](#cite_note-06-23-22-478) adopting her mother's surname because she no longer wished to be associated with Musk.[\[471\]](#cite_note-06-23-22-478)

Musk began dating English actress [Talulah Riley](/wiki/Talulah_Riley "Talulah Riley") in 2008.[\[472\]](#cite_note-479) They married two years later at [Dornoch Cathedral](/wiki/Dornoch_Cathedral "Dornoch Cathedral") in Scotland.[\[473\]](#cite_note-marriage-480)[\[474\]](#cite_note-481) In 2012, the couple divorced, then remarried the following year.[\[475\]](#cite_note-talulah-482) After briefly filing for divorce in 2014,[\[475\]](#cite_note-talulah-482) Musk finalized a second divorce from Riley in 2016.[\[476\]](#cite_note-483) Musk then dated the American actress [Amber Heard](/wiki/Amber_Heard "Amber Heard") for several months in 2017;[\[477\]](#cite_note-484) he had reportedly been "pursuing" her since 2012.[\[478\]](#cite_note-hollywood-485)

In 2018, Musk and Canadian musician [Grimes](/wiki/Grimes "Grimes") confirmed they were dating.[\[479\]](#cite_note-486) Grimes and Musk have three children, born in 2020, 2021, and 2022.[\[h\]](#cite_note-491) Musk and Grimes originally gave their eldest child the name "X [Æ](/wiki/%C3%86 "Æ") A-12", which would have violated California regulations as it contained characters that are not in the modern English alphabet;[\[484\]](#cite_note-492)[\[485\]](#cite_note-493) the names registered on the birth certificate are "X" as a first name, "Æ A-[Xii](/wiki/Roman_numerals "Roman numerals")" as a middle name, and "Musk" as a last name.[\[486\]](#cite_note-494)[\[487\]](#cite_note-xaea-xii.cnet-495) They received criticism for choosing a name perceived to be impractical and difficult to pronounce;[\[488\]](#cite_note-496) Musk has said the intended pronunciation is "X Ash A Twelve".[\[487\]](#cite_note-xaea-xii.cnet-495) Their second child was born via [surrogacy](/wiki/Surrogacy "Surrogacy").[\[489\]](#cite_note-GrimesVanityFair2022-497) Despite the pregnancy, Musk confirmed reports that the couple were "semi-separated" in September 2021; in an interview with [_Time_](/wiki/Time_\(magazine\) "Time (magazine)") in December 2021, he said he was single.[\[490\]](#cite_note-498)[\[491\]](#cite_note-499) In October 2023, Grimes sued Musk over parental rights and custody of X Æ A-Xii.[\[492\]](#cite_note-500)[\[493\]](#cite_note-501)[\[494\]](#cite_note-502) Elon Musk has taken X Æ A-Xii to multiple official events in Washington, D.C. during [Trump's second term in office](/wiki/Second_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "Second presidency of Donald Trump").[\[495\]](#cite_note-503)

Also in July 2022, _The Wall Street Journal_ reported that Musk allegedly had an affair with [Nicole Shanahan](/wiki/Nicole_Shanahan "Nicole Shanahan"), the wife of Google co-founder [Sergey Brin](/wiki/Sergey_Brin "Sergey Brin"), in 2021, leading to their divorce the following year.[\[496\]](#cite_note-504) Musk denied the report.[\[497\]](#cite_note-505) Musk also had a relationship with Australian actress [Natasha Bassett](/wiki/Natasha_Bassett "Natasha Bassett"), who has been described as "an occasional girlfriend".[\[498\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson20237,_265-506) In October 2024, _The New York Times_ reported Musk bought a Texas compound for his children and their mothers,[\[499\]](#cite_note-507) though Musk denied having done so.[\[500\]](#cite_note-508)

Musk also has four children with [Shivon Zilis](/wiki/Shivon_Zilis "Shivon Zilis"), director of operations and special projects at [Neuralink](/wiki/Neuralink "Neuralink"): twins born via [IVF](/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation "In vitro fertilisation") in 2021, a child born in 2024 via surrogacy and a child born in 2025.[\[i\]](#cite_note-515)

On February 14, 2025, [Ashley St. Clair](/wiki/Ashley_St._Clair "Ashley St. Clair"), an influencer and author, posted on X claiming to have given birth to Musk's son Romulus five months earlier, which media outlets reported as Musk's supposed thirteenth child.[\[j\]](#cite_note-519) On February 22, 2025, it was reported that St Clair had filed for sole custody of her five-month-old son and for Musk to be recognised as the child's father.[\[510\]](#cite_note-520)[\[511\]](#cite_note-521) On March 31, 2025, Musk wrote that, while he was unsure if he was the father of St. Clair's child, he had paid St. Clair $2.5 million and would continue paying her $500,000 per year.[\[k\]](#cite_note-527) Later reporting from the _Wall Street Journal_ indicated that $1 million of these payments to St. Clair were structured as a loan.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Mattioli_16APR2025-2)

### Involvement with Jeffrey Epstein

See also: [List of people named in the Epstein files](/wiki/List_of_people_named_in_the_Epstein_files "List of people named in the Epstein files")

In 2014, Musk and [Ghislaine Maxwell](/wiki/Ghislaine_Maxwell "Ghislaine Maxwell") appeared together in a photograph taken at an Academy Awards after-party, which Musk later described as a "[photobomb](/wiki/Photobombing "Photobombing")".[\[517\]](#cite_note-528)[\[21\]](#cite_note-:13-23) The January 2026 [Epstein files](/wiki/Epstein_files "Epstein files") contain emails between Musk and Epstein from 2012 to 2013, after [Epstein's first conviction](/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein#First_criminal_case_\(2005–2011\) "Jeffrey Epstein").

Emails released on January 30, 2026, indicated that Epstein invited Musk to visit his private island on multiple occasions.[\[518\]](#cite_note-529) The correspondence showed that while Epstein repeatedly encouraged Musk to attend, Musk did not visit the island. In one instance, Musk discussed the possibility of attending a party with his then-wife [Talulah Riley](/wiki/Talulah_Riley "Talulah Riley") and asked which day would be the "wildest party"; according to the emails, the visit did not take place after Epstein later cancelled the plans.[\[l\]](#cite_note-535)

On [Christmas day](/wiki/Christmas_day "Christmas day") in 2012, Musk emailed Epstein asking "Do you have any parties planned? I've been working to the edge of sanity this year and so, once my kids head home after Christmas, I really want to hit the party scene in [St Barts](/wiki/St._Barts "St. Barts") or elsewhere and let loose. The invitation is much appreciated, but a peaceful island experience is the opposite of what I'm looking for".[\[524\]](#cite_note-RobinsEarly2026-536) Epstein replied that the "ratio on my island" might make Musk's wife uncomfortable to which Musk responded, "Ratio is not a problem for Talulah".[\[524\]](#cite_note-RobinsEarly2026-536)

On September 11, 2013, Epstein sent an email asking Musk if he had any plans for coming to New York for the opening of the [United Nations General Assembly](/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly "United Nations General Assembly"), saying that many "interesting people" would be coming to Epstein's house. Musk responded that "Flying to NY to see UN diplomats do nothing would be an unwise use of time".[\[525\]](#cite_note-Rascius2026-537) Epstein responded by stating "Do you think i am retarded. Just kidding, there is no one over 25 and all very cute."[\[525\]](#cite_note-Rascius2026-537)

Musk has denied any close relationship with Epstein and described him as a "creep" who attempted to ingratiate himself with influential people.[\[21\]](#cite_note-:13-23) When Musk was asked in 2019 if he introduced Epstein to [Mark Zuckerberg](/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg "Mark Zuckerberg"), Musk responded: "I don't recall introducing Epstein to anyone, as I don't know the guy well enough to do so."[\[525\]](#cite_note-Rascius2026-537) The released emails nonetheless showed cordial exchanges on a range of topics, including Musk's inquiry about parties on the island.[\[522\]](#cite_note-theguardian.com-533)[\[526\]](#cite_note-538)[\[21\]](#cite_note-:13-23) The correspondence also indicated that Musk suggested hosting Epstein at SpaceX, while Epstein separately discussed plans to tour SpaceX and bring "the girls", though there is no evidence that such a visit occurred.[\[527\]](#cite_note-539) Musk has described the release of the files a "distraction", later accusing the [second Trump administration](/wiki/Second_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "Second presidency of Donald Trump") of suppressing them to protect powerful individuals, including Trump himself.[\[m\]](#cite_note-543)

Wealth
------

.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}

These paragraphs are an excerpt from [Wealth of Elon Musk](/wiki/Wealth_of_Elon_Musk "Wealth of Elon Musk").\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wealth_of_Elon_Musk&action=edit)\]

Elon Musk is the wealthiest person in the world, with an estimated [net worth](/wiki/Net_worth "Net worth") of US$636 billion as of March 2026, according to the _[Bloomberg Billionaires Index](/wiki/Bloomberg_Billionaires_Index "Bloomberg Billionaires Index")_,[\[531\]](#cite_note-544) and $809 billion according to _[Forbes](/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_,[\[532\]](#cite_note-545) primarily from his ownership stakes in [SpaceX](/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX") and [Tesla](/wiki/Tesla,_Inc. "Tesla, Inc.").

Having been first listed on the [_Forbes Billionaires List_](/wiki/The_World%27s_Billionaires "The World's Billionaires") in 2012,[\[533\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_:1-546) around 75% of Musk's wealth was derived from Tesla stock in November 2020,[\[534\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_gates-547) although he describes himself as "[cash poor](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cash_poor "wikt:cash poor")".[\[535\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_cash-548)[\[536\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_wsj-549) According to _Forbes_, he became the first person in the world to achieve a net worth of $300 billion in 2021; $400 billion in December 2024;[\[537\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_maruf-550) $500 billion in October 2025;[\[538\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_Elon_$500M_Forbes-551) $600 billion in mid-December 2025;[\[539\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_$600B-552) $700 billion later that month;[\[540\]](#cite_note-553) and $800 billion in February 2026.[\[541\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_$800B-554)

In November 2025, a Tesla pay package worth potentially $1 trillion for Musk was approved, which he is to receive over 10 years if he meets specific goals.[\[542\]](#cite_note-Wealth_of_Elon_Musk_$1_trillion_package_approved-555)

### Musk Foundation

Main article: [Musk Foundation](/wiki/Musk_Foundation "Musk Foundation")

The Musk Foundation is a United States–based charitable [foundation](/wiki/Foundation_\(nonprofit\) "Foundation (nonprofit)") funded and directed primarily by Musk. The foundation is dedicated to promoting [renewable energy](/wiki/Renewable_energy "Renewable energy"), [crewed space exploration](/wiki/Space_exploration "Space exploration"), [pediatrics](/wiki/Pediatrics "Pediatrics"), science and engineering education, and the "development of safe [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") for the benefit of humanity".[\[543\]](#cite_note-secretive_foundation-556)

At the end of 2024, the Musk Foundation had over $14 billion in assets. Since 2020, donations have largely been sent to organizations affiliated with Musk and his businesses.

Public image
-

Main article: [Public image of Elon Musk](/wiki/Public_image_of_Elon_Musk "Public image of Elon Musk")

Although his ventures have been highly influential within their separate industries starting in the 2000s, Musk only became a public figure in the early 2010s. He has been described as an eccentric who makes spontaneous and impactful decisions, while also often making controversial statements, contrary to other billionaires who prefer reclusiveness to protect their businesses. Musk's actions and [his expressed views](/wiki/Views_of_Elon_Musk "Views of Elon Musk") have made him a polarizing figure.[\[544\]](#cite_note-Trouble-557) Biographer [Ashlee Vance](/wiki/Ashlee_Vance "Ashlee Vance") described people's opinions of Musk as polarized due to his "part philosopher, part [troll](/wiki/Troll_\(slang\) "Troll (slang)")" persona on Twitter.[\[545\]](#cite_note-celebrity-558) He has drawn denouncement for using his platform to mock the self-selection of [personal pronouns](/wiki/Preferred_gender_pronoun "Preferred gender pronoun"),[\[546\]](#cite_note-559) while also receiving praise for bringing international attention to matters like [British](/wiki/British_people "British people") survivors of [grooming gangs](/wiki/Grooming_gangs_scandal "Grooming gangs scandal").[\[547\]](#cite_note-560)

Musk has been described as an American [oligarch](/wiki/Oligarchy "Oligarchy") due to his extensive influence over public discourse, social media, industry, politics, and government policy.[\[548\]](#cite_note-561) After Trump's re-election, Musk's [influence and actions](/wiki/Political_activities_of_Elon_Musk#United_States "Political activities of Elon Musk") during the transition period and the [second presidency of Donald Trump](/wiki/Second_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "Second presidency of Donald Trump") led some to call him "President Musk", the "actual president-elect", "shadow president" or "co-president".[\[549\]](#cite_note-562)[\[550\]](#cite_note-563)

### Accolades

Main article: [List of awards and honors received by Elon Musk](/wiki/List_of_awards_and_honors_received_by_Elon_Musk "List of awards and honors received by Elon Musk")

[![Musk wearing a medal](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Conectividade_e_Prote%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Amaz%C3%B4nia_com_Elon_Musk_-_52089866211.png/250px-Conectividade_e_Prote%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Amaz%C3%B4nia_com_Elon_Musk_-_52089866211.png)](/wiki/File:Conectividade_e_Prote%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Amaz%C3%B4nia_com_Elon_Musk_-_52089866211.png)

Musk receiving the [Order of Defence Merit](/wiki/Order_of_Defence_Merit "Order of Defence Merit") from the [Brazilian Armed Forces](/wiki/Brazilian_Armed_Forces "Brazilian Armed Forces") in 2022[\[551\]](#cite_note-Costa2022-564)

Awards for his contributions to the development of the [Falcon rockets](/wiki/Falcon_rocket "Falcon rocket") include the [American Institute of Aeronautics and Astronautics](/wiki/American_Institute_of_Aeronautics_and_Astronautics "American Institute of Aeronautics and Astronautics") George Low Transportation Award in 2008,[\[552\]](#cite_note-565) the [Fédération Aéronautique Internationale](/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_A%C3%A9ronautique_Internationale "Fédération Aéronautique Internationale") Gold Space Medal in 2010,[\[553\]](#cite_note-566) and the [Royal Aeronautical Society](/wiki/Royal_Aeronautical_Society "Royal Aeronautical Society") Gold Medal in 2012.[\[554\]](#cite_note-567) In 2015, he received an honorary doctorate in engineering and technology from [Yale University](/wiki/Yale_University "Yale University")[\[555\]](#cite_note-568) and an [Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers Honorary Membership](/wiki/IEEE_Honorary_Membership "IEEE Honorary Membership").[\[556\]](#cite_note-569) Musk was elected a [Fellow of the Royal Society](/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society "Fellow of the Royal Society") (FRS) in 2018.[\[557\]](#cite_note-570)[\[n\]](#cite_note-572) In 2022, Musk was elected to the [National Academy of Engineering](/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering "National Academy of Engineering").[\[559\]](#cite_note-lat20141214-573)

_[Time](/wiki/Time_\(magazine\) "Time (magazine)")_ has listed Musk as [one of the most influential people in the world](/wiki/Time_100 "Time 100") in 2010,[\[560\]](#cite_note-574) 2013,[\[561\]](#cite_note-575) 2018,[\[562\]](#cite_note-576) and 2021.[\[563\]](#cite_note-577) Musk was selected as _Time_'s "[Person of the Year](/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year "Time Person of the Year")" for 2021. Then _Time_ editor-in-chief [Edward Felsenthal](/wiki/Edward_Felsenthal "Edward Felsenthal") wrote that, "Person of the Year is a marker of influence, and few individuals have had more influence than Musk on life on Earth, and potentially life off Earth too."[\[564\]](#cite_note-578)[\[565\]](#cite_note-579)

Notes

1.  **[^](#cite_ref-1 "Jump up")** While Musk is affiliated with his proposed [America Party](/wiki/America_Party "America Party"), it is not yet an official political party under the FEC.
2.  **[^](#cite_ref-3 "Jump up")** Only 14 of Musk's children are publicly known. _[The Wall Street Journal](/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ reported in 2025 that sources close to Musk suggest that the true number of Musk's children is much higher.[\[1\]](#cite_note-Mattioli_16APR2025-2) One of the 14, Nevada Alexander Musk, is deceased.
3.  **[^](#cite_ref-86 "Jump up")** Musk remained on the board and served as an advisor.[\[82\]](#cite_note-84)[\[83\]](#cite_note-vance89-85)
4.  **[^](#cite_ref-118 "Jump up")** SpaceX received nearly $900 million in [Federal Communications Commission](/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission "Federal Communications Commission") subsidies for Starlink.[\[113\]](#cite_note-116)[\[114\]](#cite_note-117)
5.  **[^](#cite_ref-187 "Jump up")** He did not file the necessary SEC paperwork within 10 days of his stake passing 5%, a violation of US securities laws and the centerpiece of a current [SEC investigation and lawsuit](/wiki/SEC_investigation_into_the_acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "SEC investigation into the acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk") against him.[\[182\]](#cite_note-twitter_buy-186)
6.  **[^](#cite_ref-303 "Jump up")** The "Roman salute" is a gesture which was used by [Italian Fascists](/wiki/Italian_Fascist "Italian Fascist"), then adopted by the Nazis. It is not believed to have been used by ancient Romans.[\[297\]](#cite_note-302)
7.  **[^](#cite_ref-414 "Jump up")** Musk stated he was considering taking Tesla private at a price of $420 a share, an alleged reference to [marijuana](/wiki/Cannabis_\(drug\) "Cannabis (drug)").[\[405\]](#cite_note-411) Members of Tesla's board and rapper [Azealia Banks](/wiki/Azealia_Banks "Azealia Banks") alleged that Musk may have been under the influence of recreational drugs when he wrote the tweet.[\[406\]](#cite_note-412)[\[407\]](#cite_note-413)
8.  **[^](#cite_ref-491 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[480\]](#cite_note-487)[\[481\]](#cite_note-488)[\[482\]](#cite_note-489)[\[483\]](#cite_note-490)
9.  **[^](#cite_ref-515 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[501\]](#cite_note-Zilis-509)[\[502\]](#cite_note-510)[\[503\]](#cite_note-NYTTAU-511)[\[504\]](#cite_note-WhoIs-512)[\[505\]](#cite_note-513)[\[506\]](#cite_note-514)
10.  **[^](#cite_ref-519 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[1\]](#cite_note-Mattioli_16APR2025-2)[\[507\]](#cite_note-516)[\[508\]](#cite_note-517)[\[509\]](#cite_note-518)
11.  **[^](#cite_ref-527 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[512\]](#cite_note-522)[\[513\]](#cite_note-523)[\[514\]](#cite_note-524)[\[515\]](#cite_note-525)[\[516\]](#cite_note-526)
12.  **[^](#cite_ref-535 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[519\]](#cite_note-e-530)[\[520\]](#cite_note-531)[\[521\]](#cite_note-Robins-Early-532)[\[21\]](#cite_note-:13-23)[\[522\]](#cite_note-theguardian.com-533)[\[523\]](#cite_note-:4-534)
13.  **[^](#cite_ref-543 "Jump up")** Attributed to mutliple sources:[\[528\]](#cite_note-WSJ-timeline2-540)[\[523\]](#cite_note-:4-534)[\[529\]](#cite_note-doj-541)[\[530\]](#cite_note-:14-542)
14.  **[^](#cite_ref-572 "Jump up")** In 2024, Musk's [Royal Society](/wiki/Royal_Society "Royal Society") membership was criticized by 74 members over his alleged anti-scientific behavior and promotion of misinformation, prompting debates about the society's standards on membership and leading to the resignation of [Dorothy Bishop](/wiki/Dorothy_V._M._Bishop "Dorothy V. M. Bishop"), a neuropsychologist at the [University of Oxford](/wiki/University_of_Oxford "University of Oxford"), who cited her dissatisfaction with the Society's response.[\[558\]](#cite_note-571)

45.  **[^](#cite_ref-47 "Jump up")** [Vance (2017)](#Vance), pp. 43–44. _What rarely gets mentioned is that Musk attended the University of Pretoria for five months before heading off on his grand adventure. ... Musk characterized the time at university as just something to do while he awaited his Canadian documentation._
46.  **[^](#cite_ref-48 "Jump up")** [Vance (2017)](#Vance), p. 45. _After a 1,900-mile bus ride, he ended up in Swift Current, a town of fifteen thousand people. Musk called a second cousin out of the blue from the bus station and hitched a ride to his house._

48.  **[^](#cite_ref-50 "Jump up")** [Vance (2017)](#Vance), p. 46. _Musk spent the next year working a series of odd jobs around Canada. He tended vegetables and shoved out grain bins at a cousin's farm located in the tiny town of Waldeck. ... He inquired about the job with the best wage, which turned out to be a gig cleaning the boiler room of a lumber mill for eighteen dollars an hour._

52.  ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](#cite_ref-Vance368_54-0) [_**b**_](#cite_ref-Vance368_54-1) [Vance (2017)](#Vance), p. 368. _Musk produced a document for me dated June 22, 2009, that came from Judith Haccou, the director of graduate admissions in the office of the registrar at Stanford University. It read, "As per special request from my colleagues in the School of Engineering, I have searched Stanford's admission data base and acknowledge that you applied and were admitted to the graduate program in Material Science Engineering in 1995. Since you did not enroll, Stanford is not able to issue you an official certification document." Musk also had an explanation for the weird timing on his degrees from Penn. "I had a History and an English credit that I agreed with Penn that I would do at Stanford," he said. "The I put Stanford on deferment. Later, Penn's requirements changed so that you don't need the English and History credit. So they awarded me the degree in '97 when it was clear I was not going to go to grad school, and their requirement was no longer there."_

O'Reilly also subpoenaed the registrar's office at Stanford to verify Musk's admittance in 1995 for his doctorate work in physics. ["Judge finds Elon Musk likely acted unconstitutionally in shuttering USAID"](https://thehill.com/regulation/court-battles/5201430-judge-elon-musk-usaid/). _[The Hill](/wiki/The_Hill_\(newspaper\) "The Hill (newspaper)")_. Retrieved March 18, 2025. It marks the first time a judge has ruled that Musk is likely exercising enough independent authority to require him to be confirmed by the Senate under the Constitution's Appointments Clause. "The record of his activities to date establishes that his role has been and will continue to be as the leader of DOGE, with the same duties and degree of continuity as if he was formally in that position,'" wrote Chuang, an appointee of former President Obama. Chuang rejected the Trump administration's argument that Musk is not the DOGE administrator and is instead merely a senior adviser to the president who has no independent authority.

Further reading
-

*   [Conger, Kate](/wiki/Kate_Conger "Kate Conger"); [Mac, Ryan](/wiki/Ryan_Mac "Ryan Mac") (2024). [_Character Limit: How Elon Musk Destroyed Twitter_](/wiki/Character_Limit:_How_Elon_Musk_Destroyed_Twitter "Character Limit: How Elon Musk Destroyed Twitter") (1st hardcover ed.). New York: Penguin Press. [ISBN](/wiki/ISBN_\(identifier\) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0593656136](/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0593656136 "Special:BookSources/978-0593656136"). [OCLC](/wiki/OCLC_\(identifier\) "OCLC (identifier)") [1432234243](https://search.worldcat.org/oclc/1432234243).
*   [Farrow, Ronan](/wiki/Ronan_Farrow "Ronan Farrow") (August 28, 2023) \[August 21, 2023 (online)\]. ["Elon Musk's Shadow Rule"](https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2023/08/28/elon-musks-shadow-rule). A Reporter at Large (story series). _[The New Yorker](/wiki/The_New_Yorker "The New Yorker")_. Retrieved August 25, 2023.
*   Tarnoff, Ben, ["Ultra Hardcore"](https://www.nybooks.com/articles/2024/01/18/ultra-hardcore-elon-musk-walter-isaacson/) (subscription required) (review of [Walter Isaacson](/wiki/Walter_Isaacson "Walter Isaacson"), _Elon Musk_, Simon and Schuster, 2023, 670 pp.), _[The New York Review of Books](/wiki/The_New_York_Review_of_Books "The New York Review of Books")_, vol. LXXI, no. 1 (January 18, 2024), pp. 6, 8, 10. "There is an anti-modern impulse to Musk, a craving for lordship that can't be entirely satisfied within the confines of a capitalist economy. A king doesn't have advertisers or shareholders or customers, and Musk, if he continues on his current trajectory, may very well be abandoned by all three. [Aristotle](/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") says a good ending should be surprising but inevitable. It's possible to imagine multiple finales for Musk that meet these criteria, but the story always begins the same way. Once upon a time in [Pretoria](/wiki/Pretoria "Pretoria"), there was a boy who wanted to be a man." (p. 10.)
